Borsuk v. Town of St. John


No. 45S03-0405-CV-00236


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


820 N.E.2d 118; 2005 Ind. LEXIS 1



January 4, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Lake Superior Court, No. 45D01-0011-MI-33. The Honorable Diane Kavadias Schneider, Judge. On Petition to Transfer from the Indiana Court of Appeals, No. 45A03-0305-CV-196.
Borsuk v. Town of St. John, 800 N.E.2d 217, 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 2339 (Ind. Ct. App., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, ab owner and a trustee, sought review of the judgment of the Lake Superior Court (Indiana) finding that defendant town did not err in denying the request by the owner and trustee to rezone half of their parcel so that the entire parcel was zoned as commercial. The matter was transferred from the Indiana Court of Appeals on a petition to transfer after the Indiana Court of Appeals ordered the town to rezone the parcel.


OVERVIEW: The owner petitioned the town's plan commission to rezone the entire parcel for commercial use, as the owner intended to build a gas station. Opponents to the rezoning testified about existing traffic congestion in the area and expressed concerns that rezoning would aggravate the situation and would compromise safety. They favored road construction to fix the traffic problem before any new commercial development. The local comprehensive plan envisioned commercial zoning of the entire parcel at some point in the future. The commission denied the rezoning. Under Ind. Code Ann. § 36-7-4-603, the commission was to pay reasonable regard to a number of factors, only one of which was the comprehensive plan. Contrary to the argument of the owner and trustee, the town did not ignore the comprehensive plan. The commission and the town council determined that traffic congestion in the area had to be addressed before rezoning occurred. This issue, combined with concerns for nearby property values, provided a rational basis for the town's decision. Although these concerns did not address the comprehensive plan, it did not follow that the town ignored this factor.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

130 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


McManus v. State


No. 82S00-0104-DP-188


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


814 N.E.2d 253; 2004 Ind. LEXIS 780



August 31, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by McManus v. State, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 107 (Ind., Jan. 28, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by McManus v. Indiana, 546 U.S. 831, 126 S. Ct. 53, 163 L. Ed. 2d 83, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 6178 (2005)
Post-conviction proceeding at State v. McManus, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 496 (Ind., June 27, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with three counts of murder. During trial, defendant became ill and made various motions for mistrial, all of which were denied. The jury found defendant guilty as charged and recommended a death sentence. The Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana) sentenced defendant to death and denied his motion to correct errors. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that Indiana's death penalty statute in effect at the time of his sentencing violated the Sixth and Eighth Amendments. In upholding the statute's constitutionality, the supreme court concluded that the statute's requirement that the jury find at least one aggravating circumstance in order to recommend the death penalty met the requirements of Ring and Apprendi and that instructing the jury that its sentence recommendation was not binding did not unconstitutionally lead the jury to feel less responsible than it should for the sentencing decision. Defendant also contended that the trial court erred in denying his motions for a mistrial because he was incompetent to stand trial. The supreme court found no clear error in the trial court's decision, noting that there was testimony that the medications defendant was on assisted him in participating in his trial and were not used to medicate a diagnosed psychosis. Finally, the supreme court found defendant's death sentence to be appropriate. The supreme court noted that the aggravating factors, the commission of multiple murders and the age of the children, outweighed the mitigating factors.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

131 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


M-Plan, Inc. v. Ind. Comprehensive Health Ins. Ass'n


No. 49S02-0312-CV-605


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


809 N.E.2d 834; 2004 Ind. LEXIS 530



June 8, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion Superior Court, No. 49D07-0207-PL-1136. The Honorable Gerald S. Zore, Judge. On Petition for Transfer from the Indiana Court of Appeals, No. 49A02-209-CV-759.
M-Plan, Inc. v. Ind. Comprehensive Health Ins. Ass'n, 784 N.E.2d 546, 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 353 (Ind. Ct. App., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff health maintenance organizations (HMO) challenged a decision dismissing their declaratory judgment action against defendants, the Indiana Comprehensive Health Insurance Association (ICHIA) and the Commissioner of Insurance, for a declaration that ICHIA's assessments were improper. The Indiana Court of Appeals reversed that dismissal and the case was transferred for review.


OVERVIEW: The HMOs were members of the ICHIA and were required to help contribute to the ICHIA's losses. The HMOs argued the ICHIA's assessment methods allocated a disproportionate share of ICHIA's losses to the HMOs and the HMOs sought a declaratory judgment that the methods were improper. The trial court dismissed the action, but the lower appellate court reversed that dismissal. The court found that whether the ICHIA was viewed as a private association or a state agency, exhaustion of its internal remedies, including appeals to the ICHIA and the Commissioner, was required before a member HMO could resort to litigation to challenge an assessment. While the HMOs argued that even if the doctrine of exhaustion of administrative remedies applied, exceptions to that doctrine excused exhaustion. The court found the HMOs did not suggest that either ICHIA or the Commissioner was powerless to effect a remedy, so futility was not available. The court also rejected the HMOs other exception arguments because they raised issues best left to an initial determination by the ICHIA.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the HMOs' action.

 

132 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Ritchie v. State


No. 49S00-0011-DP-638


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


809 N.E.2d 258; 2004 Ind. LEXIS 476



May 25, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Ritchie v. Indiana, 546 U.S. 828, 126 S. Ct. 42, 163 L. Ed. 2d 76, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 6128 (2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at Ritchie v. State, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 996 (Ind., Nov. 8, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion Superior Court, No. 49G04-0010-CF-172900. The Honorable Patricia Gifford, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Trial court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was convicted of murdering a police officer, appealed his conviction and sentence of the death penalty by the Marion Superior Court (Indiana). Because the victim was a law enforcement officer, the prosecutor sought the death penalty. Defendant argued, inter alia, that Ind. Code § 35-50-2-9 (2003) was unconstitutional. Defendant also challenged the sufficiency of the evidence that he had the requisite mens rea to commit murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot the police officer while he was trying to escape on foot after stealing a van. The appellate court held there was no merit to the contention that lethal injection was a per se violation of the Eighth Amendment. Ind. Code § 35-50-2-9 was not unconstitutional. The changes in § 35-50-2-9 which occurred after defendant was charged were procedural in nature for purposes of the ex post facto doctrine. The jurors' weighing of mitigating and aggravating factors was not required to be done under a reasonable doubt standard. Once a statutory aggravator was found by the jury beyond a reasonable doubt, the Sixth Amendment was satisfied. There was no evidence of prosecutorial misconduct in regard to charging a witness with a crime. It was within the trial court's discretion to determine that a reference to a tattoo in violation of a court order was not so prejudicial as to warrant a new trial. Shooting a handgun, even if merely shooting backwards without stopping and aiming, in an effort to "slow down" a pursuing officer met the test of "knowing" for purpose of a murder conviction. The mere fact that a juror was upset with defendant's attorney did not warrant a new trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Barker


No. 49S00-0308-DP-392


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


809 N.E.2d 312; 2004 Ind. LEXIS 477



May 25, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing granted by State v. Barker, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 425 (Ind., May 4, 2005)
Adhered to, On reconsideration by, Remanded by State v. Barker, 826 N.E.2d 648, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 402 (Ind., May 4, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Interlocutory Appeal from the Marion Superior Court, No. 49G05-9308-CF-95544. The Honorable Grant W. Hawkins, Judge.
State v. Barker, 768 N.E.2d 425, 2002 Ind. LEXIS 341 (Ind., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Trial court order reversed; remanded for reinstatement of the death penalty request.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed an interlocutory appeal from an order of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) dismissing the State's request for the death penalty and ordering a sentencing proceeding where a term of years was the only question. Defendant's death sentence was imposed after a jury found him guilty of two counts of murder and one count each of kidnapping, confinement, burglary, and carrying a handgun without a license.


OVERVIEW: The State contended that the trial court erred in concluding that, because it did not require a penalty phase jury to find that mitigating circumstances outweigh aggravating circumstances beyond a reasonable doubt, the Indiana death penalty statute was unconstitutional. The State's appeal argued that weighing was not a fact that required proof beyond reasonable doubt. It also urged that the requirement for a jury to find beyond a reasonable doubt any fact that made a murder defendant eligible for the death penalty applied only to aggravating circumstances under the Indiana scheme. The supreme court concluded that the trial court erred and that there was no constitutional requirement that the weighing factor be found beyond a reasonable doubt. As for defendant's contention that the trial court's finding that Ind. Code § 35-50-2-9(f) was unconstitutional should have been affirmed because the statute unconstitutionally permitted a death sentence to be imposed by a judge alone in cases where the jury could not reach a sentencing decision, the supreme court concluded that the statute was not unconstitutional as written and thus, did not impede the State's request for the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the case was remanded for reinstatement of the death penalty request.

State v. Ben-Yisrayl


No. 49S00-0308-PD-391


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


809 N.E.2d 309; 2004 Ind. LEXIS 478



May 25, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Yisaryl, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 366 (Ind., Apr. 13, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Ben-Yisrayl v. Indiana, 546 U.S. 1020, 126 S. Ct. 659, 163 L. Ed. 2d 533, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 8453 (2005)
On remand at, Remanded by Ben-Yisrayl v. State, 908 N.E.2d 1223, 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 949 (Ind. Ct. App., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Interlocutory Appeal from the Marion Superior Court, No. CR84-076E. The Honorable Grant W. Hawkins, Judge.
Davis v. State, 598 N.E.2d 1041, 1992 Ind. LEXIS 203 (Ind., 1992)



DISPOSITION: Trial court's order reversed; remanded for reinstatement of death penalty request.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed an interlocutory appeal from the judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) which held the death penalty statute, Ind. Code § 35-50-2-9, was unconstitutional; dismissed the State's request for the death penalty; and remanded for a sentencing hearing where a term of years was the only available option for defendant, who was convicted of murder, burglary, and rape.


OVERVIEW: In a post-conviction proceeding, the death sentence was vacated due to ineffective assistance of penalty-phase counsel and remanded for a new penalty phase trial. On remand, the trial court granted defendant's motion to dismiss the death penalty request. It concluded that Ind. Code § 35-50-2-9 was unconstitutional because it permitted a sentence of death without requiring the jury to find beyond a reasonable doubt that the aggravating circumstance or circumstances outweighed any mitigating circumstances, which the trial court believed violated Apprendi. The State contended that the trial court erred in concluding that, because it did not require a penalty-phase jury to find that mitigating circumstances outweighed aggravating circumstances beyond a reasonable doubt, the Indiana death penalty statute was unconstitutional. The appellate court held that § 35-50-2-9 did not violate the Sixth Amendment as interpreted by Apprendi and Ring. Because the weighing factor did not need to be found beyond a reasonable doubt, the omission of such a requirement in § 35-50-2-9(l) did not render the statute unconstitutional. The trial court erred in its conclusion to the contrary.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the matter was remanded for reinstatement of the death penalty request.

Helsley v. State


No. 63S00-0303-CR-103


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


809 N.E.2d 292; 2004 Ind. LEXIS 471



May 25, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by, Judgment entered by Helsley v. State, 2015 Ind. LEXIS 827 (Ind., Sept. 24, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Pike Circuit Court, No. 63C01-0104-CF-231. The Honorable Lee F. Baker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision entered by the Pike Circuit Court (Indiana) that convicted him of two counts of murder and sentenced him to life without parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed various errors in his appeal: (1) admission of evidence from unlawful searches of his vehicle and residence; (2) admission of cumulative and inflammatory photographs; (3) unconstitutional ex post facto application of the penalty statute amendment; and (4) misleading sentence modification instruction. Addressing defendant's first argument, the court found that based on the facts presented to the trial court and the rational and reasonable inferences drawn from them, where was a sufficient basis to allow a reasonable person to conclude that a search of defendant's vehicle and his residence would have uncovered evidence of a crime. The search warrant was supported by adequate probable cause. The court also found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by admitting 10 photographs into evidence of the murder scene and the victims. The court found that the 2002 amendment to the penalty statute did not violate the Ex Post Facto Clause, and therefore the trial court was required to sentence defendant in accordance with the jury's recommendation of life imprisonment without parole. The court found that the sentence instruction was not misleading.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

 

136 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Saylor v. State


No. 48S00-9712-PD-647


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


808 N.E.2d 646; 2004 Ind. LEXIS 464



May 21, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Madison Superior Court, No. 48D03-9206-CF-185. The Honorable Fredrick R. Spencer, Special Judge.
Saylor v. State, 686 N.E.2d 80, 1997 Ind. LEXIS 142 (Ind., 1997).



DISPOSITION: Case remanded to the trial court with instructions to enter a sentence of sixty years for murder, twenty years for robbery and twenty years for confinement, all to be served consecutively.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of murder, robbery, and confinement, and was sentenced to death. The convictions and sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. Defendant then sought post-conviction relief. The Madison Superior Court (Indiana) denied post-conviction relief, and that denial was affirmed. Defendant then sought rehearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to death despite a unanimous jury recommendation otherwise. At the time of the trial and direct appeal, the judge was authorized to override a jury recommendation if the statutory aggravating circumstances outweighed any mitigating circumstances. Since then, the United States Supreme Court decided Apprendi, and the Indiana general assembly amended Indiana's death penalty statute to remove the authority to impose death if the jury recommended against it. It was unnecessary for the appellate court to rule on the retroactivity of these changes. Under Ind. Const. art. VII, § 4 and Ind. R. App. P. 7(B), the appellate court had the power to review and revise sentences. Even if the Sixth Amendment did not bar defendant's execution, defendant, if tried currently, could not be sentenced to death without a jury recommendation that death be imposed. The death sentence was thus inappropriate and was revised. At the time of defendant's crime, the punishment of life without parole was unavailable, and a term of years was required. Two death penalty aggravating circumstances were found, and the mitigating circumstances were entitled to little weight.


OUTCOME: The sentence was revised. The case was remanded to the trial court with instructions to enter a sentence of 60 years for murder, 20 years for robbery, and 20 years for confinement, all to be served consecutively.

SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


808 N.E.2d 652; 2004 Ind. LEXIS 472

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Lake Superior Court case no. 2CR-133-886-531.
Williams v. State, 793 N.E.2d 1019, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 614 (Ind., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Petition for rehearing and subsequently-filed requests for substantive relief from the conviction and sentence DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant applied for reconsideration of the denial of his petition under Ind. Code § 35-50-2-9(k) (2003) in which defendant sought to challenge a judgment from the Lake Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted him for murder and sentenced him to death. Defendant also made other motions, including several requests to supplement the record with additional materials and for funds to conduct additional investigation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to death for multiple murders committed during a robbery. Since that conviction, defendant had the convictions and the sentence reviewed on the merits by a state trial court in his first post-conviction proceeding, twice on appeal by the court, and by all three levels of the federal judiciary. The United States Supreme Court declined to hear his case three times. Defendant made a final petition under Ind. Clark v. State

SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


808 N.E.2d 1183; 2004 Ind. LEXIS 460

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Madison Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted him of murder and sentenced him to life without parole under Ind. Code § 35-50-2-9 (1992).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of shooting into an inhabited dwelling after a scuffle with one of the occupants, murdering one victim, and attempting to murder another. Code § 35-50-2-9(b); and (4) the jury's finding beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant intentionally discharged a firearm into an inhabited dwelling satisfied Ring and Apprendi.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction but remanded for entry of a corrected sentencing order.

Worman Enters. v. Boone County Solid Waste Mgmt. Dist.


No. 06S01-0306-CV-254


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


805 N.E.2d 369; 2004 Ind. LEXIS 227



March 9, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Boone Superior Court, No. 06D01-0011-CP-390. The Honorable Ora A. Kincaid, III, Judge. On Petition To Transfer from the Indiana Court of Appeals, No. 06A01-0206-CV-202.
Worman Enters. v. Boone County Solid Waste Mgmt. Dist., 779 N.E.2d 565, 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 2043 (Ind. Ct. App., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a company, sued defendant, an agency, alleging that the agency did not have the authority to issue a permit to operate solid waste facilities and clean fill sites, and that the permitting process was unlawful because of ex parte communications between the agency and private citizens. The Boone Superior Court (Indiana) granted the agency's summary judgment motion. The company appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The company's facility processed trees, brush, leaves, grass, and dirt, and sold the resultant mulch. The company also processed concrete and bricks and sold the resultant stone. The management district was created by Ind. Code art. 13-21 to regulate solid waste management in the area. The management district claimed that the company's operation was an illegal and unpermitted site. The parties initially agreed to engage in a permit application process before the company brought the instant action. The company argued that because the conduct regulated in the permit was regulated by the Indiana Department of Environmental Management, the agency's power to regulate the company's facility was preempted by Ind. Code § 36-1-3-8(a)(7) (1998). The court held that the Indiana Home Rule Act did not prohibit solid waste management districts from regulating solid waste. The specific grant of authority in the Solid Waste Management District Act governed over the general terms of the Home Rule Act. The court further held that the prohibitions against ex parte communications that applied to administrative agencies and to courts did not apply to the management district.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment was affirmed.

Ind. Dep't of Natural Res. v. Newton County


No. 37S00-0206-CV-330


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


802 N.E.2d 430; 2004 Ind. LEXIS 89



January 29, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Jasper Superior Court, No. 37D01-0004-OV-33. The Honorable J. Phillip McGraw, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Trial court judgment reversed; case remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee county sued appellant state natural resources department, contending that a sale of land to the department was void as in violation of the Newton County, Indiana, Farm Preservation Ordinance, and the Newton County, Indiana, Land Acquisition Notice Act. The Jasper Superior Court (Indiana) set aside the land sale and found that Ind. Code § 14-22-8-7(c) (1998) was unconstitutional. The department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Farm Preservation Ordinance and the Land Acquisition Notice Act imposed requirements on purchases of land in the county by governmental agencies, and the acquisition at issue did not follow the dictated procedures. The trial court found that the sale violated the ordinances, and that Ind. Code § 14-22-8-7(c) (1998) of the Game Bird Habitat Act was unconstitutionally vague. The appellate court held that the Home Rule Act, Ind. Code § 36-1-3-1 (1998) et seq., expressly prohibited the imposition of duties on other units of local government. The Game Bird Habitat Act expressly granted the department the authority to acquire land to achieve its purposes, and the ordinances sought to regulate the state in that activity. This was not within the county's power. The legislature did not need to supply more specific definitions for the terms "willing seller" and "game bird habitat" in Ind. Code § 14-22-8-7(c) (1998) to guide the department. There was no doubt that the property owner was a willing seller. There was no evidence that the department interpreted the terms "game bird" or "habitat" improperly with respect to the acquisition.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed. The case was remanded with instructions to dismiss the county's complaint.

Baugh v. State


No. 29S02-0301-CR-22


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


801 N.E.2d 629; 2004 Ind. LEXIS 40



January 15, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Companion case at Henke v. State, 801 N.E.2d 633, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 41 (Ind., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Hamilton Superior Court, No. 29D04-0102-DF-858. The Honorable J. Richard Campbell, Judge. On Petition To Transfer from the Indiana Court of Appeals, No. 29A02-0202-CR-167.
Baugh v. State, 781 N.E.2d 1141, 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 2194 (Ind. Ct. App., 2002)
Baugh v. State, 778 N.E.2d 498, 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1840 (Ind. Ct. App., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The case was transferred from the Court of Appeals of Indiana reversing the trial court's convictions of defendant for operating a motor vehicle with a specific amount of alcohol in the body, operating while intoxicated, and operating while intoxicated within five years of a previous conviction for the same offense. In the process, the appellate court determined that Ind. Code § 35-21-2-1(i) (2000) was unconstitutional as applied to defendant.


OVERVIEW: The road on which defendant was driving drunk formed the boundary between two counties, the county in which the trial court sat and another county. The boundary was the middle of the road. Although the side of the road on which defendant was travelling when he drove drunk was in the other county, charges were brought in the trial court's county. Defendant asserted on appeal that Ind. Code § 35-32-2-1(i) (2000), which provided for venue in either county when the crime occurred on a highway bordering two counties, was unconstitutional. Defendant asserted that he had a right under Ind. Const. art. I, § 13 and Ind. Code § 35-32-2-1(a) (2000) to be tried in the county where the offense was committed. The reviewing court found that Ind. Code § 35-32-2-1(i) was constitutional. The legislature was permitted to establish concurrent venue for violations on or near county borders. Defendant's drunk driving had a sufficient nexus with the trial court's jurisdiction for defendant to be tried there. Defendant's dangerous operation of the vehicle on one side of the road endangered those on the other side of the road as well.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Henke v. State


No. 29S05-0401-CR-27


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


801 N.E.2d 633; 2004 Ind. LEXIS 41



January 15, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Hamilton Superior Court, No. 29D04-0012-CM-7823. The Honorable J. Richard Campbell, Judge. On Petition To Transfer from the Indiana Court of Appeals, No. 29A05-0211-CR-554.
Baugh v. State, 801 N.E.2d 629, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 40 (Ind., Jan. 15, 2004)
Henke v. State, 792 N.E.2d 970, 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1490 (Ind. Ct. App., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in Hamilton Superior Court (Indiana) with operating a vehicle while intoxicated, operating a vehicle with a blood alcohol content of .15 or more, and operating a vehicle with a blood alcohol content of .08 or more. Defendant moved to dismiss. The trial court denied the motion. On interlocutory appeal, the Indiana Court of Appeals reversed. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: All charges were based on defendant's driving in the eastbound lanes of a street where that street formed the boundary between Marion and Hamilton Counties. The parties agreed for the purposes of the appeal that the eastbound lanes were in Marion County and that defendant drove only in Marion County. Defendant argued that Ind. Code § 35-32-2-1(i) (2000) was unconstitutional as applied to ham, and that as the evidence was clear that defendant never crossed the border into another county, the Indiana Constitution limited venue to the county where the driving occurred. The trial court held that the venue statute conferred venue on Hamilton County. The appellate court found that the statute could not confer venue over crimes where the evidence pointed to only one county as the location of the offense. The supreme court found that concurrent venue was constitutional for offenses committed by operating a vehicle on a highway forming the boundary between two counties.


OUTCOME: The supreme court granted transfer, affirmed the trial court in the interlocutory appeal, and remand the case for further proceedings.

D & M Healthcare v. Kernan


No. 49S05-0310-CV-437


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


800 N.E.2d 898; 2003 Ind. LEXIS 1101



December 17, 2003, Decided  
December 17, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion Superior Court, No. 49D06-0205-PL-000846. The Honorable Thomas J. Carroll, Judge.

On Petition To Transfer from the Indiana Court of Appeals, No. 49A05-0301-CV-26.
D & M Healthcare, Inc. v. O'Bannon, 793 N.E.2d 241, 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1458 (Ind. Ct. App., 2003).



DISPOSITION: Trial court judgment affirmed; decision of Court of Appeals superseded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs nursing homes sought a declaratory judgment that certain legislation became law despite the governor's veto. The trial court entered judgment in favor of defendant governor, but the Court of Appeals (Indiana) reversed. The governor sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The nursing homes said the veto was ineffective because the governor's veto message was delivered to the legislature six months before Ind. Const. art. V, § 14(a)(2)(D) called for it to be returned. The supreme court held its interest in previously vetoed judicial pay raise legislation, which its decision would affect, normally precluded participation in the case, but there was no one else to decide the case. The governor's veto was sustained. Under the de minimis doctrine, there were no practical consequences of the governor's delivery of the vetoed bill to the legislature before the legislature reconvened, rather than on that date. The veto message met the objective of art. V, § 14(a)(2)(D) of assuring the legislature would have the earliest possible opportunity to consider the veto. The veto substantially conformed to the constitutionally prescribed process, so it was properly returned to the legislature. Section 14 put a deadline on the governor's physical return of vetoed legislation to the legislature, when it was not in session, but allowed it to be done at any time, as long as the result was a return on the first day of the next legislative session.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

144 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Embry v. O'Bannon


No. 49S02-0310-CV-479


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


798 N.E.2d 157; 2003 Ind. LEXIS 904



October 29, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion Circuit Court, No. 49C01-0001-CP-120.

On Petition To Transfer from the Indiana Court of Appeals, No. 49A02-0112-CV-863. The Honorable William Lawrence, Judge.
Embry v. O'Bannon, 770 N.E.2d 943, 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1050 (Ind. Ct. App., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Trial court's grant of summary judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted plaintiff taxpayers' petition for transfer of their appeal from an affirmance, by the Indiana Court of Appeals, of a trial court's summary judgment denying relief in a constitutional challenge to defendant state officials' promulgation of an interpretation of Ind. Code § 21-3-1.6-1.1 as allowing a dual enrollment process in determining public school entitlement to state aid, arguing that it violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 6.


OVERVIEW: Section 21-3-1.6-1.1 allowed school districts, in determining their average daily membership of students for state funding purposes, to count (proportionately, under a subsequent amendment) students in private, including parochial, schools in their figures. The taxpayers argued that this practice allowed religious schools to save money by not spending money on staff and positions in such areas as computer science and foreign languages. The high court first held that the taxpayers had standing under Indiana's public standing doctrine. Nonetheless, their appeal failed. Looking to the history of Ind. Const. art. I, § 6, to Indiana case law interpreting it, and to case law in other states interpreting nearly identical provisions, the high court held that the fact that a law conferred a purely incidental benefit on a religiously oriented institution was not grounds for invalidating it. The public schools benefited financially, and an incidental result was that parochial schools saved on certain expenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment.

 

145 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Leone v. State


No. 28S00-0206-CR-327


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


797 N.E.2d 743; 2003 Ind. LEXIS 853



October 22, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Greene Circuit Court, No. 28C01-0012-CF-101. The Honorable David K. Johnson, Judge Direct Appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a plea of guilty, the Indiana trial court found defendant guilty of felony murder, but mentally ill. Defendant was sentenced to life in prison without parole based on two statutory aggravating circumstances, torture and intentional killing while attempting or committing child molestation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the State failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt the existence of the aggravating circumstance of torture. Although defendant's actions were despicable, the supreme court found that they did not exceed the scope of murder or molestation. Defendant did not attempt to coerce the victim through torturous acts, nor did he appear to indulge in sadistic acts. Defendant also contended that the trial court abused its discretion in weighing various mitigating and aggravating circumstances. Defendant alleged that the trial court gave inadequate weight to several of the circumstances it found as mitigating. The supreme court found no error noting, inter alia, that although statutory mitigators did exist, no credible evidence was sufficient to excuse of explain defendant's behavior. Finally, defendant argued that he was sentenced to life without parole under a facially and structurally unconstitutional statutory sentencing scheme. The supreme court noted that with his plea of guilty, defendant forfeited claimed entitlement to certain rights including that of a jury trial. Thus, contrary to defendant's argument, his sentence did not conflict with Apprendi or Ring.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

146 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Humphreys v. Clinic for Women, Inc.


No. 49S00-0011-CV-714


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


796 N.E.2d 247; 2003 Ind. LEXIS 795; 118 A.L.R.5th 771



September 24, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion Superior Court, No. 49D12-9908-MI-1137. The Honorable Susan Macey Thompson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted direct review under Ind. R. App. P. 4 of an appeal by defendants, the Indiana Family and Social Services Administration and its administrator, from a summary judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) that granted a motion by plaintiff health care providers for summary judgment, holding that Ind. Code §§ 12-15-5-1 and 16-34-1-2 and a related regulation violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 23.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to its obligation not to violate federal Medicaid reimbursement guidelines, Indiana's legislature enacted Ind. Code §§ 12-15-5-1(17) and 16-34-1-2, and the Administration promulgated Ind. Admin. Code tit. 405, r. 5-28-7, which defined abortions as medically necessary and covered by Medicaid only if performed to preserve the patient's life or in situations involving rape or incest. The high court applied Indiana's Collins standard in determining whether the disparate treatment accorded different pregnant women was reasonably related to inherent characteristics that distinguished the classes, and found no manifest unreasonableness in the distinctions. It also found that the standards were uniformly applicable to the various women who fell into the class. Nonetheless, the court found a violation of Ind. Const. art. I, § 23 in the scheme as applied, because, while Indiana health care law generally protected women whose bodily functions would be severely threatened by continued pregnancy (as by diabetes or hypertension) just as it protected those whose lives were threatened, they were not protected in the area of Medicaid coverage.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in part, finding the statutory scheme constitutional on its face, but also affirmed in part, finding the scheme unconstitutional as applied.

Dvorak v. City of Bloomington


No. 53S01-0209-CV-472


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


796 N.E.2d 236; 2003 Ind. LEXIS 791



September 23, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Monroe Circuit Court, No. 53C04-9604-OV-350. The Honorable Elizabeth N. Mann, Judge.
Dvorak v. City of Bloomington, 768 N.E.2d 490, 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 694 (Ind. Ct. App., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted appellee city's petition to transfer after the Court of Appeals (Indiana) reversed a trial court's decision, which had upheld Bloomington, Ind., Mun. Code § 20.02.01.00. The court of appeals held § 20.02.01.00 unconstitutional under the Privileges and Immunities Clause of the Indiana Constitution, Ind. Const. art. 1, § 23.


OVERVIEW: The city filed a complaint against appellants, a property owner and his tenants, claiming that they violated Bloomington, Ind., Mun. Code § 20.02.01.00, which prohibited the owner's property from being occupied by more than four adults unrelated by blood, marriage, or adoption. Appellants claimed that the ordinance was void as an ultra vires act and violative of Ind. Const. art. 1, § 23. A trial court denied the motion and after an appeal and remand, upheld the ordinance. The court of appeals reversed, finding the ordinance unconstitutional under § 23. The court held that the ordinance did not violate § 23, nor was it void as an ultra vires act exceeding the city's authority. The court held that there was no § 23 violation because the ordinance was uniformly applicable and equally available to all persons similarly situated. Limiting multiple-adult households in single family residential zones to families, and excluding non-families, was reasonably related to the difference between families and non-families. The court further held that, considering the enabling legislation, Ind. Code § 36-7-4-201 et seq., and the Home Rule Act, the adoption of the ordinance was not ultra vires.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Ind. Dep't of Envtl. Mgmt. v. Twin Eagle L.L.C.


No. 49S00-0204-CV-237


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


798 N.E.2d 839; 2003 Ind. LEXIS 794



September 23, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion Superior Court, No. 49F12-0107-CP-002490. The Honorable Michael D. Keele, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Indiana Department of Environmental Management (IDEM) sought review of the grant of summary judgment by the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) in favor of appellee developer. The trial court held, among other things, that Indiana state environmental laws gave the IDEM no National Pollutant Discharge Elimination System (NPDES) regulatory authority over private ponds or isolated wetlands that were not waters of the United States.


OVERVIEW: The developer sought to undertake a project that would put dredged and fill material in certain wetlands and waters on a particular site where the developer planned to construct a residential development on approximately 460 acres of property it owned. Approximately 21.52 acres of the property consisted of ponds and wetlands. Of those 21.52 acres, 14.75 of them were wetlands and private ponds that were not subject to the Clean Water Act (CWA). The material was a "pollutant" as the term was used in the CWA and Indiana environmental regulations. The appellate court held the trial court had subject matter jurisdiction over the declaratory judgment action. The IDEM was within its statutory authority to require NPDES permits for the discharge of fill material into waters of the state. The IDEM could regulate private ponds when the discharges from the ponds caused or threatened to cause water pollution. Some isolated wetlands were waters of the state.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the court's grant of summary judgment in favor of the developer. The appellate court left it to the regulatory process to determine in the first instance whether permits were required and, if so, whether they should be issued. The matter was remanded to the trial court with directions to enter a declaratory judgment.

Majors v. Abell


Indiana Supreme Court Cause No. 94S00-0303-CQ-94


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


792 N.E.2d 22; 2003 Ind. LEXIS 613



July 24, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Answer conformed to Majors v. Abell, 2004 U.S. App. LEXIS 4813 (7th Cir. Ind., Mar. 15, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE UNITED STATES COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE SEVENTH CIRCUIT. The Honorable William J. Bauer, Senior Circuit Judge. The Honorable Richard A. Posner, Circuit Judge. The Honorable Frank H. Easterbrook, Circuit Judge. Cause No. 02-2204.
Majors v. Abell, 317 F.3d 719, 2003 U.S. App. LEXIS 1004 (7th Cir. Ind., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Certified question answered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, persons who wanted to take out advertisements advocating the election or defeat of particular candidates, filed an action in federal court against defendants, various state and local election officials, challenging the constitutionality of Ind. Code § 3-9-3-2.5 (Supp. 2001). The U.S. Court of Appeals for the Seventh Circuit asked the state supreme court to interpret § 3-9-3-2.5(b)(1), (d).


OVERVIEW: Persons who wanted to take out advertisements advocating the election or defeat of particular candidates filed an action in federal district court, challenging the constitutionality of provisions in Ind. Code § 3-9-3-2.5 (Supp. 2001) which required persons who distributed political advertising that expressly advocated the election or defeat of a clearly identified candidate to identify persons who paid for the advertising. The district court dismissed the action, but the U.S. Court of Appeals for the Seventh Circuit held that the trial court's decision that non-candidate plaintiffs lacked standing to challenge the statute was incorrect, and it certified the following question to the state supreme court: was the term "person" in § 3-9-3-2.5(b)(1), (d) limited to candidates, authorized committees, and the agents of such committees, or did it have a broader scope? The state supreme court held that the term "person" in § 3-9-3-2.5(b), (d) was not limited to candidates, authorized political committees or subcommittees of candidates, and the agents of such committees or subcommittees, but included any individual or organization.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court answered the question that was certified by the federal court of appeals.

Doe v. O'Connor


Supreme Court No. 49S00-0301-CV-1


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


790 N.E.2d 985; 2003 Ind. LEXIS 574



June 26, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49D03-0211-PL-001935. The Honorable Patrick L. McCarty, Judge.
Doe v. O'Connor, 781 N.E.2d 672, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 2 (Ind., 2003).



DISPOSITION: Stay dissolved; trial court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a convicted sex offender, appealed from the denial by the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) of his request for a preliminary injunction to enjoin the inclusion of the offender's information in the Indiana Sex and Violent Offender Directory (2003 Directory) and the county sheriffs' registry (Sheriffs' Registry). At the offender's request, the implementation of the 2003 Directory and the Sheriffs' Registry had been stayed pending appeal.


OVERVIEW: The offender claimed that he had a constitutional right to a hearing on whether he posed any danger to society before his information was posted in the 2003 Directory and the Sheriffs' Registry. The offender withdrew his federal constitutional challenge. The appellate court held that the offender did not have a due process right under Ind. Const. art. I, § 12 to a hearing to determine his current dangerousness as his dangerousness was not material under the statute. The legislature had determined that the registry information of all sex offenders, currently dangerous or not, had to be publicly disclosed. Any harsh consequences arising out of the registration laws were a matter for the legislature. The same reasoning was applied to the offender's privacy argument under Ind. Const. art. I, § 1. The dangerousness of the offender was not material to the registration requirement, and the offender was not entitled to a hearing to determine his current dangerousness based on constitutional privacy concerns under the Indiana Constitution.


OUTCOME: The stay was dissolved. The judgment was affirmed.

 

151 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Stroud v. Lints


Indiana Supreme Court Cause No. 20S04-0306-CV-275


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


790 N.E.2d 440; 2003 Ind. LEXIS 536



June 25, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Stroud v. Lints, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 966 (Ind., Nov. 13, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ELKHART CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Terry C. Shewmaker, Judge. Cause No. 20C01-9806-CT-038. Indiana Court of Appeals Cause No. 20A04-0010-CV-458.
Stroud v. Lints, 760 N.E.2d 1176, 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 27 (Ind. Ct. App., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court's opinion was superseded, trial court's judgment was affirmed, in part, vacated, in part, and case was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, a circuit court awarded compensatory damages and punitive damages to plaintiffs, the parents of an injured teenager, in a personal injury action filed against defendant driver. The driver appealed the punitive damages award. The court granted transfer after the Court of Appeals (Indiana) affirmed the punitive damages award, finding that it did not constitute an abuse of discretion.


OVERVIEW: The driver was 17 years old. As a result of the accident, he pleaded guilty to criminal charges and was sentenced to eight years' imprisonment. The trial court awarded plaintiffs $ 500,000 in punitive damages in addition to $ 1.4 million in compensatory damages. The driver argued that the punitive damages award was excessive, and the court agreed. The standard of review to be applied in Indiana on a state law challenge to punitive damages was de novo review, just as it would be if a federal due process challenge was made. The factors involved in evaluating a federal constitutional challenge to a punitive award were the same as were relevant to a state law review, so that for consistency, the same standard of review was proper. Applying de novo review to the punitive damages award against the driver, it was clearly excessive. The driver's financial position was a factor to be considered in awarding punitive damages. The driver could never hope to pay the punitive damages award, which was "staggering." While such damages were meant to deter and punish, the award against the driver passed the point of deterrence and punishment long before it reached the $ 500,000 mark.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against the driver insofar as it awarded compensatory damages. The court vacated the award of punitive damages and remanded the case to the trial court for entry of a punitive damages award in an amount reflecting proper consideration of the driver's financial status.

State ex rel. Cittadine v. Ind. DOT


No. 20S03-0306-CV-260


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


790 N.E.2d 978; 2003 Ind. LEXIS 535



June 24, 2003, Decided  
June 24, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ELKHART SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable L. Benjamin Pfaff, Judge. Cause No. 20D01-008-CP-00547.
State ex rel. Cittadine v. Ind. DOT, 750 N.E.2d 893, 2001 Ind. App. LEXIS 1225 (Ind. Ct. App., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court's opinion was superseded and trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Indiana Court of Appeals found that petitioner lacked standing to bring an action to enforce a statute requiring railroads to maintain public crossings so motorists would have a certain unobstructed view of railroad tracks and, thus, affirmed the trial court's denial of petitioner's application for a permanent writ of mandamus. The state supreme court granted transfer to address the availability of the public standing doctrine.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner filed a petition for writ of mandamus to require respondent state transportation agency to enforce a statute against respondent railroad and any other railroad violating a statute that required railroads to maintain public crossings under their control in such a manner as to allow motorists to have an unobstructed view for a certain distance. The trial court denied his petition for writ of mandamus. After petitioner appealed, the appellate court affirmed the trial court's ruling. It found that petitioner lacked standing to bring the action because he did not have a personal stake in the outcome and could not show that he had suffered, or was in immediate danger of suffering, a direct injury as a result of the conduct violating the statute. The state supreme court granted transfer to acknowledge the availability of the public standing doctrine. It then found that petitioner's claim involved the enforcement of a public right, and thus the claim was cognizable under the public standing doctrine. However, the state supreme court affirmed the trial court's denial of the request for the writ of mandamus because amendment of the statute had made the controversy moot.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court disagreed with the appellate court and concluded that petitioner's claim was cognizable under the public standing doctrine, but agreed with and affirmed the trial court's denial of petitioner's request for a permanent writ of mandamus on the ground that amendment of the relevant statute made the controversy moot.

 

153 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Cheatham v. Pohle


Indiana Supreme Court Cause No. 40S01-0209-CV-471


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


789 N.E.2d 467; 2003 Ind. LEXIS 440



May 30, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Indiana Court of Appeals Cause No. 40A01-0010-CV-329. APPEAL FROM THE JENNINGS SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Carl Taul, Special Judge. Cause No. 40D01-9803-CP-143.
Cheatham v. Pohle, 764 N.E.2d 272, 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 338 (Ind. Ct. App., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant husband distributed at least 60 copies of explicit photos of plaintiff, his ex-wife. The wife sued, alleging invasion of privacy and intentional infliction of emotional distress. A jury awarded her both compensatory and punitive damages. The trial court entered judgment. Both parties appealed. The Indiana Court of Appeals affirmed. The State intervened, and its petition for rehearing was denied. Its petition to transfer was granted.


OVERVIEW: The husband's arguments were not preserved for appeal, leaving only the wife's challenges to the constitutionality of the punitive damages allocation statute, Ind. Code § 34-51-3-6 (1998). Under that statute, a punitive damage award was paid to the clerk of court, who then distributed 25 percent to the party to whom the damages were awarded and 75 percent to the state treasurer. The highest appellate court found that civil plaintiffs had no absolute right to receive punitive damages, as they were a creature of the common law. The Indiana Legislature was free to create, modify, or abolish common law causes of action. Although the State paid no part of the attorney's fee, there was no State demand for the attorney's services. The attorney was not required to represent his client in the instant action if the attorney did not want to. No attorney could be compelled to pursue a punitive damage claim. There was no unconstitutional taking of 75 percent of the wife's punitive damages award because a lawyer and a client took the hand that the legislature dealt them, no more and no less. The statute did not require the attorney to provide services to the State without just compensation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Griffith v. State


Supreme Court Cause No. 41S00-0109-CR-438


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


788 N.E.2d 835; 2003 Ind. LEXIS 412



May 16, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE JOHNSON CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable K. Mark Loyd, Judge. Cause No. 41C01-0005-CF-00114.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State charged defendant with two counts of murder, one count of burglary as a Class B felony, and one count of arson, a Class B felony. Defendant moved to suppress his confession. The motion was denied. A jury found him guilty of all counts. The Johnson Circuit Court (Indiana) sentenced defendant to life without parole for the murders, and two consecutive 18-year sentences for the counts of burglary and arson. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court should have suppressed his confession because it was the product of a warrantless arrest without probable cause. The appellate court found no error, since the arresting officers had probable cause to believe that defendant committed the crimes. Defendant also asserted that the delay between his arrest and the probable cause hearing violated his constitutional rights. The State acknowledged that the detention for 63 hours prior to a probable cause hearing was unreasonable. The appellate court found, however, that defendant's confession did not occur until after he saw the magistrate. Thus, defendant's confession was not the product of the delay and was properly suppressed. Finally, defendant contended that his confession should have been suppressed because the court did not appoint counsel for him during the probable cause hearing or when he confessed, in violation of the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. Defendant did not contend he suffered any damage; thus, denial of the request to suppress was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and the sentences imposed were affirmed.

Allied Signal, Inc. v. Ott


Supreme Court No. 02S04-0111-CV-599


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


785 N.E.2d 1068; 2003 Ind. LEXIS 267; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P16,567



March 25, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Ott v. AlliedSignal, Inc., 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 884 (Ind. Ct. App., May 19, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ALLEN SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Stanley A. Levine, Judge. Cause No. 02D01-9910-CP-2074.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was reversed and case was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee widow sued appellant asbestos sellers, claiming that her husband's death was caused by his exposure to asbestos. The Allen Superior Court (Indiana) ruled that Ind. Code § 34-20-3-2 did not apply to the asbestos sellers, but because it did not, Ind. Code § 34-20-3-1 was unconstitutional. The asbestos sellers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The decedent's asbestos exposure occurred over an extended period of time. The asbestos sellers argued that they were not in the limited class to which Ind. Code § 34-20-3-2 applied, and that the widow was required to proceed under the more restrictive Ind. Code § 34-20-3-1. The widow argued that if Ind. Code § 34-20-3-2 did not allow her to proceed, then Ind. Code § 34-20-3-1 violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 12 and Ind. Code § 34-20-3-2 violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 23. The appellate court ruled that Ind. Code § 34-20-3-2 only applied if the defendant mined and sold commercial asbestos. Other defendants were entitled to the 10 year statute of repose in Ind. Code § 34-20-32-1. Application of the statute of repose would be constitutional if the first exposure occurred more than 10 years after delivery of the product. The statute might be unconstitutional if the illness could have been diagnosed within the 10 year repose period, but the decedent had no reason to know of the illness until the 10 year period expired. This was to be examined on remand. If there was an Ind. Const. art. I, § 23 defect in Ind. Code § 34-20-3-1, asbestos plaintiffs did not suffer any harm.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

Harris v. A.C. & S., Inc.


Supreme Court No. 45S03-0303-CV-125


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


785 N.E.2d 1087; 2003 Ind. LEXIS 268; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P16,568



March 25, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Jeffery J. Dywan, Judge. Cause Nos. 45D01-9812-CT-992, 45D01-9609-CT-896.

APPEAL FROM THE VIGO SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Dexter L. Bolin, Judge. Cause No. 84D03-9604-CT-652, 84D03-9604-CT-653.
Harris v. A.C. & S., Inc., 766 N.E.2d 383, 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 9 (Ind. Ct. App., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court's opinion was superseded, trial court's judgment was vacated and case was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In cases consolidated for appeal, appellant asbestos victims and their survivors sued appellee asbestos merchants, seeking recovery for injury and death resulting from exposure to asbestos. The trial court found that the claims were untimely and entered summary judgment for the asbestos merchants. The Court of Appeals (Indiana) reversed. The asbestos merchants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The intermediate appellate court found that Ind. Code § 34-20-3-2 applied to this case. The appellate court ruled that Ind. Code § 34-20-3-2 applied only to entities that produced raw asbestos, while Ind. Code § 34-20-3-1 applied to those who sold asbestos-containing products. This statutory scheme was not unconstitutional except where a reasonably experienced physician could have diagnosed the plaintiff with an asbestos-related illness or disease within the 10-year statute of repose, yet the potential plaintiff had no reason to know of the condition until the 10-year period had expired. Here, since the asbestos merchants did not both mine and sell commercial asbestos, Ind. Code § 34-20-3-2 did not apply, and the Ind. Code § 34-20-3-1 general 10-year statute of repose applied. The claims were filed after the expiration of the 10 year period, so summary judgment for the asbestos merchants was proper unless a physician could have diagnosed a given plaintiff with an asbestos-related illness within the 10-year period, yet the potential plaintiff had no reason to know of the condition until the 10-year period expired. The trial court was directed to examine this on remand.


OUTCOME: The opinion of the intermediate appellate court was vacated. The judgment of the trial court was vacated and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Jurich v. Garlock, Inc.


Supreme Court No. 45S03-0303-CV-127


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


785 N.E.2d 1093; 2003 Ind. LEXIS 269; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P16,571



March 25, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Sub nomine at Jurich v. John Crane, Inc., 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 520 (Ind. Ct. App., Mar. 31, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Jeffery J. Dywan, Judge. Cause No. 45D01-9704-CT-345.
Jurich v. Garlock, Inc., 759 N.E.2d 1066, 2001 Ind. App. LEXIS 1810 (Ind. Ct. App., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court's opinion was superseded, trial court's judgment was vacated, and case was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff widow sued defendants, asbestos products distributors, in the trial court, which granted the distributors' summary judgment motions. The Indiana Court of Appeals reversed, and defendants moved for transfer pursuant to Ind. R. App. P. 58(A).


OVERVIEW: The widow's spouse was diagnosed with mesothelioma more than 10 years after he retired. The supreme court held Ind. Code § 34-20-3-1 generally applied a 10-year period of repose to products liability claims, and Ind. Code § 34-20-3-2 applied to certain asbestos liability claims. The legislature intended to subject to § 34-20-3-2 only those entities producing raw asbestos, leaving those selling asbestos-containing products, such as the distributors, within the ambit of Ind. Code § 34-20-3-1. This statutory scheme did not violate Ind. Const. art. I, §§ 12 or 23, except in the limited circumstance where a reasonably experienced physician could have diagnosed a plaintiff with an asbestos-related disease within the 10-year statute of repose, yet the plaintiff had no reason to know of the diagnosable condition until the 10-year period expired. The widow's claims, filed after the expiration of the period of repose in Ind. Code § 34-20-3-1, could not be pursued unless a reasonably experienced physician could have diagnosed her spouse with an asbestos-related disease within that period, yet the spouse had no reason to know of his condition until the period expired.


OUTCOME: Transfer was granted, the trial court's judgment was vacated, and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

Peterson v. Borst


Indiana Supreme Court Cause No. 49S02-0302-CV-71


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


786 N.E.2d 668; 2003 Ind. LEXIS 237



March 19, 2003, Decided  
March 19, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Peterson v. Borst, 789 N.E.2d 460, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 274 (Ind., Mar. 27, 2003)
Motion denied by Peterson v. Borst, 785 N.E.2d 1097, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 278 (Ind., Mar. 27, 2003)
Motion granted by Peterson v. Borst, 785 N.E.2d 1096, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 279 (Ind., Mar. 27, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Indiana Court of Appeals Cause No. 49A02-0302-CV-144. APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause Nos. 49D04-0210-MI-001844 and 49D02-0211-PL-001842.
Peterson v. Borst, 784 N.E.2d 934, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 234 (Ind., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was reversed and attached redistricting plan will govern the district boundaries of the Council unless and until a different plan is enacted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee city-county council vice president filed an action seeking a declaration that a redistricting plan he submitted was valid. Appellants, a city-county councilor and others, filed a separate action seeking an order appointing a master to assist the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) in drawing new voting district boundary lines. The superior court consolidated the actions and adopted the vice president's plan. Appellants challenged.


OVERVIEW: The City-County Council of the City of Indianapolis and Marion County (Indiana) adopted a redistricting plan proposed by the Council's vice president, after a vote along party lines. However, the mayor vetoed that plan. Instead of attempting to override the mayor's veto, the vice president filed an action in superior court, seeking a declaration that his plan was valid. The superior court consolidated that action with an action filed my members of the Council who represented the minority party, and held that the vice president's plan was valid. Sixteen judges of the superior court who voted in favor of the vice president's plan belonged to the same political party as the vice president and other members of the Council who formed the majority party in the Council, and 13 judges of the court who voted against the vice president's plan belonged to the same political party as the mayor and members of the Council who formed the minority party in Council. The state supreme court held that the superior court's ruling had the appearance that it lacked judicial neutrality and, under the circumstances, the supreme court would develop its own redistricting plan for the next election.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed the superior court's judgment adopting the vice president's redistricting plan, and ordered the use of a redistricting plan the supreme court developed, but also held that its ruling did not preclude the Council and the mayor from agreeing on a different plan.

State Bd. of Tax Comm'rs v. Ispat Inland, Inc.


Supreme Court Cause No. 49S10-0206-TA-349


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


784 N.E.2d 477; 2003 Ind. LEXIS 209



March 6, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE INDIANA TAX COURT The Honorable Thomas G. Fisher, Judge Cause No. 49T10-0107-TA-74.
Ispat Inland v. State Bd. of Tax Comm'rs, 757 N.E.2d 1078, 2001 Ind. Tax LEXIS 64 (Ind. Tax Ct., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Tax Court's ruling was reversed and Tax Court was directed to grant State Board's motion to dismiss.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a county, an assessor, and the Indiana State Board of Tax Commissioners, sought review of a decision of the Indiana Tax Court, which, upon appellee taxpayer's motion for injunctive relief, enjoined the county from outsourcing personal property audits to a third party contractor.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer protested because the assessor outsourced a personal property audit to a third party contractor. The taxpayer petitioned the Board, requesting that it interpret the property tax laws. The Board advised that the assessors could hire contractors to assess audits and the taxpayer appealed to the Tax Court. The Tax Court rejected a challenge to its subject matter jurisdiction and enjoined the county from proceeding with the audits. On appeal by the county, the assessor, and the Board, the court held that the Tax Court did not have subject matter jurisdiction to enjoin an audit being pursued by the assessor's contractor. The court held that the taxpayer had established that there was a dispute arising under the tax laws of Indiana, thus meeting the first jurisdictional requirement of Ind. Code § 33-3-5-2(a) (1996). However, there was no final determination by the Board but rather only an advisory opinion. Nor did any of the exceptions to the exhaustion requirement exist. As such, the Tax Court lacked subject matter jurisdiction under Ind. Code § 33-3-5-11(a).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the ruling of the Tax Court and directed that the Board's motion to dismiss be granted.

 

160 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Gov't Fin. v. Griffin


No. 49S10-0209-TA-489


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


784 N.E.2d 448; 2003 Ind. LEXIS 202



March 5, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE INDIANA TAX COURT The Honorable Thomas G. Fisher, Judge. Cause No. 49T10-0009-TA-98.
Griffin v. Dep't of Local Gov't Fin., 765 N.E.2d 716, 2002 Ind. Tax LEXIS 12 (Ind. Tax Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Tax court's judgment was reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer requested a refund of Indiana Hospital Care for the Indigent (HCI) taxes he paid. Respondent Indiana Department of Local Government Finance denied the request, and petitioner Lake County (Indiana) joined the taxpayer in appealing the Department's decision to the Indiana Tax Court. The tax court held that the HCI tax violated Ind. Const. art. 10, § 1, but granted the taxpayer only partial relief. Both sides sought review.


OVERVIEW: A taxpayer requested a refund of real property taxes he paid in tax years 1996 through 1998 that were assessed to support the HCI program. The Indiana Department of Local Government Finance denied the taxpayer's request, but the Indiana Tax Court found that the HCI tax violated Ind. Const. art. 10, § 1 because it was assessed at different rates in different counties, and it granted the taxpayer partial relief. The state supreme court granted review and held that (1) art. 10, § 1 required that the same tax rate be applied to everyone in a given tax district; (2) the Indiana General Assembly had the discretion to determine what constituted a tax district; and (3) the HCI tax enacted by the general assembly imposed a scheme of taxation that took into account the historical differences that existed among counties with respect to HCI costs, and it did not violate art. 10, § 1 because it allowed the tax to be assessed at different rates in different counties.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed the tax court's judgment.

 

161 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Sims v. United States Fid. & Guar. Co.


Supreme Court Cause Number: 49S02-0105-CV-229


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


782 N.E.2d 345; 2003 Ind. LEXIS 89



January 28, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Counsel Corrected January 31, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT NO. 12 The Honorable Susan Macey Thompson, Judge Cause No. 49D12-9904-CT-489. Court of Appeals Cause Number 49A02-9904-CV-295.
Appellate court's opinion: Sims v. U.S. Fid. & Guar. Co., 730 N.E.2d 232, 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 906 (Ind. Ct. App. 2000).



DISPOSITION: Appellate court's opinion was superseded and trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant worker sued appellee insurer, alleging that the insurer was grossly negligent, intentionally inflicted emotional distress, and intentionally deprived the worker of certain statutory rights by refusing to provide worker's compensation benefits and by denying him access to timely medical care and physical therapy. The trial court granted the insurer's motion to dismiss. The Court of Appeals (Indiana) reversed. The insurer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The worker claimed that the insurer had improperly denied him worker's compensation benefits. The trial court found that, under Ind. Code § 22-3-4-12.1, the Indiana Worker's Compensation Board had exclusive jurisdiction over the claims alleged. The intermediate appellate court held that Ind. Code § 22-3-4-12.1 violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 12 and Ind. Const. art. I, § 20. The appellate court ruled that there was no fundamental right to access to the courts. Rather, the legislature had the authority to modify the common law if such change did not interfere with constitutional rights. The legislature could not have unreasonably denied citizens access to the courts, but 4-12.1 Ind. Code § 22-3- 4-12.1(a) merely restricted the remedy for a breach of duty imposed on a worker's compensation carrier. Ind. Code § 22-3-4-12.1 was part of a special statutory proceeding, and not a "civil case" as contemplated by Ind. Const. art. I, § 20. The prohibition against jury trial was reasonable. Ind. Code § 22-3-4-12.1 violated neither Ind. Const. art. I, § 12 nor Ind. Const. art. I, § 20. Since its classification was reasonable, Ind. Code § 22-3-4-12.1 did not violate Ind. Const. art. I, § 23, either.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

162 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


City of S. Bend v. Kimsey


Indiana Supreme Court Cause No. 71S03-0203-CV-183


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


781 N.E.2d 683; 2003 Ind. LEXIS 17



January 15, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended January 17, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Indiana Court of Appeals Cause No. 71A03-0101-CV-13. APPEAL FROM THE ST. JOSEPH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable William C. Whitman, Judge. Cause No. 71D03-9609-CP-909.
Appellate court's opinion: City of South Bend v. Kimsey, 751 N.E.2d 805, 2001 Ind. App. LEXIS 1195 (Ind. Ct. App. 2001).



DISPOSITION: Appellate court's opinion was superseded and trial court's judgment was reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners filed a remonstrance and presented a petition in opposition to annexation by defendant city. After dismissal was denied, the city filed a counterclaim, seeking a declaratory judgment that Ind. Code § 36-4-3-13(g) (2002) was unconstitutional special legislation, in violation of Ind. Const. art. IV, § 23. The trial court found that the statute was constitutional. The Indiana Court of Appeals affirmed. Transfer was granted.


OVERVIEW: The owners' petition purportedly contained the signatures of a majority of the property owners in the proposed annexation area. This was all that was required for that particular county, under Ind. Code § 36-4-3-13(g) (2002). Since the statute applied only to counties within a specified population range, the net effect was that the opposition of 65 percent of the affected landowners, to defeat a municipal annexation, was required in 91 of Indiana's 92 counties. A simple majority was sufficient in the other. The highest appellate court found that the circumstances surrounding the enactment of the legislation led to the conclusion that the statute was special legislation. The statute's population classification served no purpose other than to identify the one county. While preserving rural land near urban areas or preventing competing annexations might be legitimate concerns, there was no basis to conclude that they were unique to the one county. Therefore, the legislation was unconstitutional special legislation. The offending part of the statute was the specified population range, set forth in Ind. Code § 36-4-3-13(g) (2002). Since it was not severable, the statute was void.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

Doe v. O'Connor


Supreme Court case no. 49S00-0301-CV-1


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


781 N.E.2d 672; 2003 Ind. LEXIS 2



January 3, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Stay dissolved by, Judgment entered by Doe v. O'Connor, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 574 (Ind., June 26, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Court of Appeals case no. 49A02-0212-CV-1083. Marion Superior Court case no. 49D03-0211-PL-1935.



DISPOSITION: Stay was entered, without bond, to maintain the status quo as it existed before the effective date of the relevant statutes and publishing of home addresses and photographs of offenders on the registries was enjoined until further order of the Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff convicted sex offenders appealed a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Indiana), which denied their motion to grant a preliminary injunction as a stay, pending appeal of a trial court's denial of the offenders' application for a preliminary injunction with respect to enforcement of certain statutes, effective January 1, 2003, that required publication of convicted sex offenders' home addresses and photographs on the Internet.


OVERVIEW: Ind. Code Ann. §§ 5-2-12-6, 36-2-13-5.5 (West Supp. 2002), effective January 1, 2003, required that the home addresses and photographs of convicted sex offenders be posted on the Internet. The offenders sought a preliminary injunction with respect to enforcement of the statutes, which the trial court denied. The court of appeals denied the motion to grant an injunction as a stay, pending appeal of the trial court's denial, and the court's consideration of the issues was sought on an expedited basis. The court accepted jurisdiction and entered a stay. The court held that the complex constitutional issues raised by the case involved numerous considerations and the balancing of various interests. Of particular note was the fact that two federal appellate courts had already decided that such Internet publication might have violated the United States Constitution. The publication was set to occur within days and the court had not had sufficient time to consider the merits. Further, the issues raised under the Indiana Constitution had never been addressed. The balance of harm favored the offenders and a stay was entered to maintain the status quo as it existed prior to the enactment.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that a stay was to be entered, without bond, to maintain the status quo as it existed before the effective date of the relevant statutes. The publishing of the home addresses and photographs of offenders on the registries was enjoined until further order of the court.

In re Wilkins


CASE NO. 49S00-0005-DI-341


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


777 N.E.2d 714; 2002 Ind. LEXIS 808



October 29, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected January 6, 2003. Modified, On rehearing: In re Wilkins, 782 N.E.2d 985, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 112 (Ind. Feb. 4, 2003).
Stay granted by, Petition for certiorari filed at In re Wilkins, 778 N.E.2d 1290, 2002 Ind. LEXIS 914 (Ind., 2002)
Later proceeding at In re Wilkins, 780 N.E.2d 842, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 1 (Ind., 2003)
Modified by, On rehearing at In re Wilkins, 782 N.E.2d 985, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 112 (Ind., 2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by WILKINS, MICHAEL A. v. DISCIPLINARY COMM'N OF IN, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 5532 (U.S., Oct. 6, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Respondent was suspended from the practice of law in Indiana for thirty days with automatic reinstatement.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a matter of original jurisdiction, petitioner disciplinary commission sought the imposition of sanctions against respondent attorney for statements made in a petition to transfer a case from the court of appeals to the supreme court.


OVERVIEW: The attorney said a court of appeals opinion left him wondering if the court was determined to find for the adverse party, and said whatever was necessary to reach that conclusion. He was charged with violating Ind. R. Prof. Conduct 8.2(a). The supreme court held while the attorney may not have authored the words, he signed the brief pursuant to Ind. R. Admis. Bar & Disc. Atty's 3(2)(d) and was jointly responsible. The attorney's other statements paraphrased bases for transfer of a case from the court of appeals to the supreme court in Ind. R. App. P. 11(b) (now Ind. R. App. P. 57) and did not violate Ind. R. Prof. Conduct 8.2(a). The statements at issue recklessly disregarded their truth or falsity concerning the integrity of a three-judge panel of the court of appeals, contrary to Rule 8.2(a). The state's interest in preserving the public's confidence in the administration of justice outweighed the attorney's freedom to air these concerns. The statement exceeded the boundaries of acceptable appellate practice. The attorney's remorse was belied by his belief that only a poor choice of words was made, and by his choice to contest the matter through available procedures.


OUTCOME: The attorney was suspended for 30 days.
