Bostick v. State


33S00-9911-CR-651


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


773 N.E.2d 266; 2002 Ind. LEXIS 657



August 19, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied January 3, 2003, Reported at: 2003 Ind. LEXIS 11.
Rehearing denied by Bostick v. State, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 11 (Ind., Jan. 3, 2003)
Subsequent appeal at Bostick v. State, 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 333 (Ind. Ct. App., Mar. 4, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE HENRY SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Michael D. Peyton, Judge. Cause No. 33D01-9807-CF-20.



DISPOSITION: On direct appeal, defendant-appellant's convictions were affirmed, sentences of life without parole were vacated, and case was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following the death of her three children, who were locked in their room during a house fire, defendant was charged with and convicted of three counts of murder and sentenced to life without parole for the three counts of murder. Upon her additional conviction of sexual misconduct with a minor, she was given a concurrent sentence of 15 years. Defendant appealed from the Henry Superior Court, (Indiana).


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that the claim that Ind. R. Evid. 704(b) was violated was not presented at trial or in defendant's pre-trial motion to exclude that was referenced in her trial objection, and thus procedural default applied. Under Ind. R. Evid. 403, police interrogators' accusations and defendant's responses had little probative value in establishing her guilt. The repeated police accusations, in the context of the entire statement, did not create a substantial risk of unfair prejudice. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting the redacted exhibits. Regardless of whether each statement was considered individually or whether all the statements were considered collectively, there was no fundamental error. The appellate court declined to infer the existence of a serious evidentiary dispute where the undisputed evidence showed that defendant's actions were done with an awareness of the high probability that they would result in the death of her children. Because of the absence of a jury determination that qualifying aggravating circumstances were proven beyond a reasonable doubt, the life sentence was vacated.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's convictions, vacated the sentences of life without parole, and remanded the case.

Moore v. State


No. 06S00-0006-PD-389


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


771 N.E.2d 46; 2002 Ind. LEXIS 563



June 26, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied November 26, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Ind. LEXIS 1012.
Rehearing denied by Moore v. State, 2002 Ind. LEXIS 1012 (Ind., Nov. 26, 2002)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Moore v. Ind., 2003 U.S. LEXIS 3506 (U.S., May 5, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE BOONE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable James R. Detamore, Judge. Cause No. 06D02-9904-CF-176.
State v. Moore, 678 N.E.2d 1258, 1997 Ind. LEXIS 42 (Ind., 1997)



DISPOSITION: Defendant's sentence of death affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to three counts of murder. The Boone Superior Court (Indiana) sentenced him to death. In 1995, defendant's petition for post-conviction relief was granted, but the State appealed, and the state supreme court reversed the post-conviction court, reinstated the guilty pleas, and remanded for a new sentencing proceeding. Defendant was once again sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant raised numerous errors. The state supreme court concluded that: (1) defendant was not deprived of his right to a jury, as he had pled guilty knowing that such a plea would deprive him of access to a jury; (2) there was probative evidence in the record from which the fact-finder could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant knew the victim was a law enforcement officer; (3) the trial court properly weighed the mitigating evidence and did not delegate that responsibility to the clemency board; (4) the length of time defendant spent on death row did not render his execution unconstitutional under either the United States or Indiana Constitutions; (5) death by lethal injection was not unconstitutional and did not involve unnecessary and wanton infliction of pain or conflict with societal norms; and (6) the trial court did not err when it excluded certain expert testimony, as that testimony would have directly reflected on defendant's intent, guilt, or innocence, and thus was an inadmissible conclusion regarding intent.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence of death was affirmed.

Dunson v. Dunson


Indiana Supreme Court Cause No. 34S02-0108-CV-370


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


769 N.E.2d 1120; 2002 Ind. LEXIS 523



June 12, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HOWARD SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Stephen M. Jessup, Judge. Cause No. 34D02-9012-DR-325. Indiana Court of Appeals Cause No. 34A02-0006-CV-375.
 Dunson v. Dunson, 744 N.E.2d 960, 2001 Ind. App. LEXIS 311 (Ind. Ct. App. 2001).



DISPOSITION: Court of appeals' judgment was affirmed, in part, reversed, in part, and case was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A trial court denied appellant minor's motion for support and educational orders against appellees, his mother and father, and granted the father's petition to find the minor emancipated under Ind. Code § 31-16-6-6(b)(3). The Indiana Court of Appeals affirmed the emancipation ruling and the denial of the support and educational orders and found that the minor waived review of a de facto custodian issue. The state supreme court granted transfer.


OVERVIEW: The minor sought the support and educational orders in 1999, alleging that appellees abandoned him. The trial court found that the minor had lived with aunts since 1996, that appellees had provided him with little support since a post-divorce agreed entry in 1998 giving them joint custody of him, and that the minor was emancipated under § 31-16-6-6(b)(3) because he had not been under appellees' care and control. The minor argued on appeal that the trial court erred in finding him emancipated and in failing to join one of his aunts as a de facto custodian under Ind. Code § 31-17-2-8.5 (Supp. 1999), and that appellees should be responsible for his appellate attorney's fees. The state supreme court held that the minor was not emancipated because his financial dependence on his extended family indicated that he was not self-supporting. The minor waived his de facto custodian argument by failing to move, pursuant to Ind. R. Trial P. 19, to join the aunt or to dismiss for lack of an indispensable party. Finally, contrary to the minor's contentions, appellees were not responsible for his appellate attorney's fees under Ind. Code § 34-10-1-2 (1998) or Ind. Code §§ 31-15-10-1, 31-16-11-1.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court summarily affirmed a finding by the court of appeals that the father waived review of a cross-appeal he had filed, reversed the conclusion that the minor was emancipated, denied the minor's request for appellate attorney's fees, affirmed the court of appeals' finding that the minor waived his de facto custodian issue, and remanded the matter to the trial court to determine if support payments for the minor were proper.

State v. Barker


Supreme Court case no. 49S00-0110-DP-461


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


768 N.E.2d 425; 2002 Ind. LEXIS 341



April 26, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by, Judgment entered by, Remanded by State v. Barker, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 477 (Ind., May 25, 2004)

DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was reversed and cause was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought interlocutory review of an order of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) declaring that Indiana's death penalty statute, Ind. Code § 35-50-2-9, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of two murders, kidnapping, confinement, burglary, and carrying a handgun without a license. The jury recommended the death penalty. The trial court followed the jury's recommendation. The death sentence was reversed on appeal, because the jury had not been instructed that life without parole was a possible sentence. Defendant moved to dismiss the death penalty request, arguing that that Indiana's death penalty statute, Ind. OUTCOME: The order was reversed and remanded.

Lake County Clerk's Office v. Smith


45S00-0102-CV-105


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


766 N.E.2d 707; 2002 Ind. LEXIS 335



April 22, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Smith v. Lake County, 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 745 (Ind. Ct. App., Apr. 27, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT, ROOM 3 The Honorable James Danikolas, Judge Cause No. 45D03-9911-CP-2969.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In this appeal from the Lake Superior Court, (Indiana), appellant sheriff et al. challenged a ruling for appellee bondsmen finding that Indiana's statutory bail scheme was unconstitutional under both the Equal Protection Clause of the United States Constitution and the Privileges and Immunities Clause of the Indiana Constitution.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that Indiana's bail scheme was not unconstitutional. The unequal treatment accorded bail agents and defendants posting 10 percent cash bonds was rationally related to the State's legitimate interest in ensuring the appearance of defendants at judicial proceedings and did not violate the Equal Protection Clause, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1. The scheme did not violate the Privileges and Immunities Clause, Ind. Const. art. I, § 23. The scheme created different classes, because without the threat of late surrender fees, bail agents had no incentive to ensure a defendant's appearance, as they got to keep the entire premium, regardless of whether the defendant appeared. Any disparate treatment between bail agents and defendants who posted 10 percent cash bonds was reasonably related to the inherent characteristics between the two unequally treated classes. Bondsmen failed to carry their burden of proving that Indiana's statutory bail scheme violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 23 or U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1.


OUTCOME: The lower court decision was reversed.

Saylor v. State


Supreme Court Cause Number 48S00-9712-PD-647


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


765 N.E.2d 535; 2002 Ind. LEXIS 221



March 20, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected March 22, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MADISON SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Fredrick R. Spencer, Special Judge. Cause No. 48D03-9206-CF-185.
Saylor v. State, 686 N.E.2d 80, 1997 Ind. LEXIS 142 (Ind., 1997)



DISPOSITION: Trial court's denial of defendant-appellant's petition for post-conviction relief was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought direct review of an order of the Madison Circuit Court (Indiana) denying post-conviction relief from a death sentence. His arguments centered on counsel ineffectiveness at every stage of the proceeding, failure to disclose exculpatory evidence, unconstitutionality of the death penalty statute, and judicial bias.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was sentenced to death, despite the jury's recommendation against it, after his murder conviction; the judgment was upheld, and then he sought post-conviction relief. The high court also found that Indiana's death penalty statute did not violate the rule of Apprendi in permitting the trial court to impose the death penalty despite a contrary recommendation, because the rule expressly excluded state death penalty statutes and because a death penalty was the permissible statutory maximum sentence for murder. Finally, the post-conviction judge's brief, casual conversation with an old friend was not grounds for disqualification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of relief.

State v. Gerschoffer


No. 71S05-0102-CR-106


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


763 N.E.2d 960; 2002 Ind. LEXIS 193



March 5, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ST. JOSEPH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable R. W. Chamblee, Judge. No. 71A05-0003-CR-116. Cause No. 71D08-9906-DF-686. Court of Appeals.

Court of appeals' opinion: State v. Gerschoffer, 738 N.E.2d 713, 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 1920 (Ind. Ct. App. 2000).



DISPOSITION: Court of appeals' opinion was superseded, trial court's grant of defendant-appellee's motion to suppress evidence was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the judgment of the Indiana Court of Appeals affirming the trial court's suppression of evidence obtained from a roadblock, where defendant was charged with operating a vehicle while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: The state police and local police department conducted a sobriety checkpoint. Defendant was pulled over. The officer smelled alcohol on defendant and noted defendant's glassy, bloodshot eyes and slurred speech. Defendant failed three sobriety tests, and his blood alcohol content was 0.11. Defendant moved to suppress all evidence obtained from the checkpoint. The appellate court found that, although checkpoints were not per se unconstitutional, the checkpoint violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 11. Factors that weighed against the constitutionality of the checkpoint included that the State failed to show that the roadblock was sufficiently related to the legitimate law enforcement purpose of combating drunk driving, the State did not provide sufficiently explicit guidance to ensure against arbitrary or inconsistent actions by the screening officers, the State failed to demonstrate that the checkpoint was avoidable, and there was no evidence that the checkpoint effectively deterred potential offenders.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

172 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Northwestern Sch. Corp. v. Linke


Supreme Court No. 34S05-0103-CV-151


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


763 N.E.2d 972; 2002 Ind. LEXIS 194



March 5, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected March 6, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE HOWARD CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Lynn Murray, Judge. Cause No. 34C01-9902-CP-131. No. 34A05-9910-CV-467. Court of Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff students brought an action against defendant school claiming that the school's policy of administering random drug tests to certain students violated the Search and Seizure Clause, Ind. Const. art. I, § 11, and the Privileges and Immunities Clause, Ind. Const. art. I, §23. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the school. The Howard Circuit Court (Indiana) reversed. The school appealed.


OVERVIEW: The students argued that the random drug testing program violated their rights under the Indiana Constitution to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures. The supreme court concluded that the drug-testing program was constitutional. The supreme court noted that the policy did not require testing for students in compulsory regular classes, but rather for those involved in voluntary activities for which they receive academic credit. The court held that the refusal to agree to drug testing which might result in forfeiture of the opportunity was not so weighty as to constitute forced consent in violation of the students' rights. As to the privileges and immunities claim, the supreme court found that the students did not carry their burden to negative every reasonable basis for random drug testing imposed upon the students. Thus, there was no violation of Ind. Const. art. I, § 23. Therefore, the supreme court held that testing those students who were at an increased risk of physical harm or were role models and leaders was reasonably related to achieving the school's purpose in providing for the health and safety of students.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Ind. Dep't of Revenue v. Adams


Supreme Court No. 49S10-0011-TA-628


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


762 N.E.2d 728; 2002 Ind. LEXIS 122



February 8, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied June 7, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Ind. LEXIS 524.
Rehearing denied by Ind. Dep't of Revenue v. Adams, 2002 Ind. LEXIS 524 (Ind., June 7, 2002)
On remand at Adams v. Ind. Dep't of Revenue, 2004 Ind. Tax LEXIS 103 (Ind. Tax Ct., Nov. 8, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE INDIANA TAX COURT. The Honorable Thomas G. Fisher, Judge. Cause No. 49T10-9904-TA-24.

Adams v. Department of State Revenue, 730 N.E.2d 840, 2000 Ind. Tax LEXIS 23 (Ind. Tax Ct. 2000)
Adams v. Dep't of State Revenue, 730 N.E.2d 840, 2000 Ind. Tax LEXIS 23 (Ind. Tax Ct., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Tax court decision reversed; remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On appeal from the Indiana Tax Court, appellant department of revenue (DOR) challenged the finding that the exclusionary rule applied to tax assessment proceedings concerning illegally seized cocaine.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that cocaine found in an unconstitutional search of the safe deposit box by criminal authorities could be used by revenue authorities to make a tax assessment. While the exclusionary rule barred the use of the cocaine as evidence in criminal proceedings, the exclusionary rule did not apply to tax assessment proceedings. There was no evidence in the record that suggested that revenue officers were involved in the search of the safe deposit box, which was the only search at issue. The costs of applying the exclusionary rule to Ind. Code § 6-7-3-13 (1998) outweighed its limited benefits in this context, and the court declined to apply the rule to the evidence seized from the safe deposit box. As to the costs, the court believed that application of the exclusionary rule in Ind. Code § 6-7-3-13 (1998) proceedings would undermine several important state interests. The police would not be significantly deterred by the prospect of the exclusion of evidence in Ind. Code § 6-7-3-13 (1998) proceedings because their primary concern was criminal prosecutions, where the exclusionary rule already applied.


OUTCOME: The tax court decision was reversed and remanded for proceedings consistent with the opinion.

 

174 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Adams v. State


Supreme Court No. 49S04-0011-CR-627


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


762 N.E.2d 737; 2002 Ind. LEXIS 123



February 8, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Court of Appeals No. 49A04-9903-CR-130. APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Z. Mae Jimison, Judge. Cause No. 49G20-9804-CF-56875.

Adams v. State, 726 N.E.2d 390, 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 509 (Ind. Ct. App. 2000) 



DISPOSITION: Trial court decision reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with dealing in cocaine, in violation of Ind. Code § 35-48-4-1 (1998), and possession of cocaine, in violation of Ind. Code § 35-48-4-6 (1998). Defendant filed a motion to suppress the cocaine, which was denied by the Marion Superior Court (Indiana). An interlocutory appeal was granted. The court of appeals reversed the trial court, and transfer was granted.


OVERVIEW: The police previously found cocaine in a safety deposit box leased by defendant, resulting in criminal charges. The charges were dropped after a trial court suppressed the cocaine for the purposes of the pending criminal charges. A day before the charges were dropped, the revenue department issued an assessment on the drugs seized from the safety deposit box, pursuant to the Controlled Substance Excise Tax, Ind. Code § 6-7-3-1 et seq. A jeopardy tax warrant was issued, and defendant's home was searched. All of the cocaine, upon which the charges in the instant case were based, was found before the police served a valid search warrant. In finding the search unreasonable, and in ordering the suppression of the cocaine, the highest appellate court found that a tax seizure could be effected without judicial intervention if the property to be seized was found in a public place. But, if it was necessary to enter private premises to effect the seizure, the government had to first obtain a court order authorizing such entry. There were no exigent circumstances, such as an attempt to abscond, hide assets, or destroy documents, which would have justified the warrantless search.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was reversed.

 

175 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Sholes v. Sholes


No. 27S02-0112-CV-655


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


760 N.E.2d 156; 2001 Ind. LEXIS 1112



December 21, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE GRANT CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Thomas R. Hunt, Judge. Cause No. 27C01-9802-DR-84. Cause No. 27A02-9906-CV-445. Indiana Court of Appeals.

Sholes v. Sholes, 732 N.E.2d 1252, 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 1213 (Ind. Ct. App. 2000) 



DISPOSITION: Transfer was granted, court of appeals' decision was reversed and cause was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee wife filed for dissolution of her marriage to appellant husband. The trial court entered a decree and divided the marital property. The trial court denied the husband's request for appointment of counsel at public expense, and denied the husband's motion to set aside the judgment. The Court of Appeals (Indiana) reversed the trial court's denial of the motion to set aside the judgment. The wife sought transfer.


OVERVIEW: The husband was serving a life sentence in prison during the case. The trial court found that the husband was without funds and ordered a transcript for appeal prepared at public expense. The intermediate appellate court held that the husband had shown that he was indigent and that all proceedings after his request for counsel were required to be vacated. The appellate court held that as a matter of statutory construction, Ind. Code § 34-10-1-2 required appointment of counsel and conferred no discretion on the trial court to deny counsel if its terms were met. The decision to appoint counsel in a civil case turned on the court's assessment of the nature of the case, the genuineness of the issues, and any other factors that bore on the wisdom of mandating public funds for that purpose. The procedure for the trial court follow was: (1) the litigant was to apply for leave to proceed as an indigent person, and (2) if the trial court found that the applicant was indigent and without sufficient means to prosecute or defend the action, the trial court was required to appoint counsel. Courts had the inherent power to appoint and require payment of counsel.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded with instructions (1) to vacate all proceedings conducted after the husband's motion to proceed as pauper, (2) determine whether the husband was indigent and without sufficient means, and (3) if so, determine whether counsel may be appointed consistent with Ind. R. Trial P. 60.5.

Monegan v. State


No. 89S00-0010-CR-600


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


756 N.E.2d 499; 2001 Ind. LEXIS 925



October 16, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE WAYNE SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 89D02-0506-CF-39. The Honorable Robert L. Reinke, Senior Judge.

Monegan v. State, 721 N.E.2d 243, 1999 Ind. LEXIS 1252 (Ind. 1999) 



DISPOSITION: Appellant's sixty-year sentence for murder affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Wayne Superior Court (Indiana) found defendant guilty of murder, and the trial court sentenced him. From an earlier appeal, the case was remanded for a resentencing. On remand, the trial court sentenced defendant to the presumptive term of 50 years and enhanced his sentence by 10 years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court failed to provide a specific statement regarding the need for correctional or rehabilitative treatment and that the court improperly considered four apprehensions that did not result in convictions. The trial court set out defendant's long history of encounters with the law, and noted various types of care and rehabilitation provided to defendant, all of which were unsuccessful. The appellate court found that the trial judge did a commendable job of explaining why an enhanced sentence was necessary. Arrests not reduced to conviction could properly be considered in sentencing as evidence that defendant's antisocial behavior had not been deterred after having been subject to the police authority, and the trial court properly considered such arrests. The trial court's consideration of defendant's prior arrests, analyzed in the way it did, and placed alongside a substantial list of convictions, was not a denial of due process. The trial court's refusal to give significant weight to defendant's age as a mitigating factor did not produce a sentence that was manifestly unreasonable. The trial court applied the correct presumptive sentencing term.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Owens Corning Fiberglass Corp. v. Cobb


Supreme Court No. 49S04-0001-CV-00033


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


754 N.E.2d 905; 2001 Ind. LEXIS 829; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P16,160



September 10, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Court of Appeals No. 49A04-9801-CV-46. APPEAL FROM THE MARION COUNTY SUPERIOR COURT, CIVIL, NO. 2. The Honorable Kenneth H. Johnson, Judge. Cause No. 49D02-9501-MI-1-47.

Original Opinion of July 22, 2001, Reported at: 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 1207.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action to recover for asbestos exposure, plaintiff personal representatives of the estate of a decedent appealed the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Indiana) which reversed a jury verdict which awarded damages to the decedent who was exposed to asbestos. Defendant asbestos manufacturer cross-appealed the denial of its pretrial motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Personal representatives of a deceased worker's estate (the estate) sought to recover damages claiming that the decedent was exposed to asbestos during the course of 40 years. The original complaint listed 33 manufacturers or distributors of asbestos, some of which settled claims. An asbestos manufacturer filed an answer which included the affirmative defense that other parties were responsible, and moved for summary judgment for lack of product identification. The trial court denied the motion, and after a trial, a jury awarded damages to the estate. Due to inadequate discovery responses, the trial court granted the estate's motion for summary judgment on the issue of other parties' liability. The intermediate court reversed, and found that the trial court should have granted the manufacturer's motion for summary judgment. The appellate court found that the estate's evidence was sufficient to establish a genuine issue of material fact as to whether the manufacturer's asbestos caused his injuries. However, the appellate court found that the trial court erred in refusing to allow the manufacturer to bring the issue of other parties' liability to the jury.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appeals court was vacated, and the trial court judgment was affirmed as to the denial of the asbestos manufacturer's motion for summary judgment. The judgment was reversed as to the grant of summary judgment on the issue of other party's liability. The judgment in favor of the estate was reversed and remanded.

State Bd. of Tax Comm'rs v. Town of St. John


No. 49S10-0009-TA-541


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


751 N.E.2d 657; 2001 Ind. LEXIS 612



July 18, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM THE INDIANA TAX COURT. Cause No. 49T10-9309-TA-70. The Honorable Thomas J. Fisher, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Decision of Tax Court reversed and directed that it deny petition for fees.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners taxpayers sought recovery of attorneys' fees incurred in pursuing litigation that successfully challenged Indiana's real property assessment procedure. The Indiana Tax Court granted the request and ordered the taxpayers to submit their proposed award, and respondent Indiana State Board of Tax Commissioners appealed.


OVERVIEW: In 1993, a municipality and various taxpayers challenged Indiana's real property assessment procedure, asserting that it did not provide a uniform and equal rate of property assessment and taxation pursuant to Ind. Const. art. X, § 1(a). Seven decisions later (two by the Supreme Court of Indiana and five by the Indiana Tax Court), the tax court ordered the Indiana State Board of Tax Commissioners to adopt new, constitutional regulations. In this action by taxpayers to recover the costs of attorneys' fees they incurred in pursuing that litigation, the tax court adopted the private attorney general exception to the American rule on payment of attorneys' fees and granted the taxpayers' request. However, the state supreme court reversed. In its opinion, the supreme court noted that the states are divided on this issue and, in Indiana, the legislature had enacted Ind. Code §§ 36-52-2-2, -3 (2001) and other statutes that provide for fee-shifting in actions involving the state or particular areas of the law. Accordingly, the supreme court refused to adopt the private attorney general exception judicially.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed the tax court's judgment and directed that the tax court deny the taxpayers petition for attorneys' fees.

Mitchell v. State


49S00-9906-CR-343


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


745 N.E.2d 775; 2001 Ind. LEXIS 300



April 16, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49G20-9601-CF-007512. The Honorable Z. Mae Jimison, Judge. 1


1 The trial and sentencing proceedings were conducted by the Honorable William E. Young, Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) convicted defendant of dealing cocaine and carrying a handgun without a license and sentenced him as a habitual offender. Defendant appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: While defendant was under police surveillance during a drug trafficking investigation, an officer observed his vehicle fail to completely stop at a stop sign. During the stop, the vehicle's passenger gave the officer a gun and two bags of marijuana. Defendant and the passenger were arrested. The officers subsequently obtained a search warrant and found a large amount of drugs, cash, and a gun in the vehicle. On appeal of defendant's convictions, the instant court affirmed. The trial court did not err by denying defendant's motion to suppress because the search and seizure did not violate his constitutional rights. The traffic stop was valid, defendant's 100-minute detention, during which a search warrant was procured, was reasonable, and the warrant was supported by probable cause, given the drugs and weapons found on the passenger and in the vehicle. Because defendant was listed as an additional driver on the vehicle's rental agreement and was the actual driver when it was stopped, the evidence was sufficient to show that he possessed the drugs.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because the trial court did not err by denying defendant's motion to suppress evidence and because the evidence was sufficient to show that defendant possessed the drugs the officers found.

City Chapel Evangelical Free Inc. v. City of South Bend


No. 71S00-0008-CV-501


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


744 N.E.2d 443; 2001 Ind. LEXIS 278



March 29, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM ST. JOSEPH CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 71C01-0002-CP-00194. The Honorable David T. Ready, Special Judge.



DISPOSITION: Remanded for hearing on City Chapel's claims under Indiana Constitution. As to denial of hearing on federal First Amendment claims, trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee city initiated proceedings to condemn for redevelopment real estate appellant used as its church meeting place. An interlocutory order of the St. Joseph Circuit Court (Indiana) overruled appellant's objections to the proceedings. Appellant requested review. Appellant requested an evidentiary hearing whether the taking violated Ind. Const. art. I and U.S. Const. amend. I protections of free exercise of religious worship and assembly.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court concluded that Indiana eminent domain laws, under which appellee sought to take appellant's property, were religious-neutral laws of general applicability so that the city was not required to demonstrate a compelling government interest. The supreme court rejected the contention that Ind. Const. art. I was to be equated with U.S. Const. amend. I. Ind. Const. art. I protected more than just the personal devotional aspect of religion; it also protected the private and communal practice of religion. Exercise of the police power of condemnation impinged upon that core value protected by Ind. Const. art. I. The appellant had the right to contest the proceedings under Ind. Code § 32-11-1-5. The supreme court ordered a hearing to determine whether appellant could carry its substantial burden to prove the condemnation materially burdened the core values of Ind. Const. art. I, §§ 2, 3, 4. The supreme court, after analysis, in a split decision, denied a hearing with respect to U.S. Const. amend. I. The hybrid claim Smith exception to the exercise of a neutral state law did not apply as the right to assemble was a derivative right of the free exercise of religion right.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the order and remanded for a hearing with respect to the Indiana Constitution claims. The court affirmed the order with respect to the United States Constitution claims.

Lambert v. State


Supreme Court No. 18S00-9702-PD-96


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


743 N.E.2d 719; 2001 Ind. LEXIS 199



March 5, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied February 19, 2002, Reported at: 2002 U.S. LEXIS 764.
Rehearing denied by Lambert v. State, 2001 Ind. LEXIS 427 (Ind., May 9, 2001)
Writ of certiorari denied Lambert v. Indiana, 534 U.S. 1136, 122 S. Ct. 1082, 151 L. Ed. 2d 982, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 764 (2002)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Lambert v. McBride, 365 F.3d 557, 2004 U.S. App. LEXIS 6658 (7th Cir. Ind., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DELAWARE SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 18D01-9101-CF-002. The Honorable Robert L. Barnet, Jr., Judge.
Lambert v. State, 675 N.E.2d 1060, 1996 Ind. LEXIS 189 (Ind., 1996)



DISPOSITION: Post-conviction court's denial of Lambert's petition for post-conviction relief affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was sentenced to death for the murder of a police officer. His conviction and sentence were upheld on direct appeal and on rehearing. Defendant petitioned for post-conviction relief and appealed the denial of that petition.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot a police officer five times in the back of the head while under arrest, handcuffed and alone in the back of the patrol car. A jury convicted defendant of murder and the trial court sentenced him to death. The appellate court found, inter alia, that in view of the nature and circumstances of the defendant and the crimes, the trial judge's comments on the coldness of the defendant, his lack of remorse, and his proclivity to kill again were entirely consistent with the considerations required to be taken into account by the judge in determining the defendant's sentence. The comments did not reflect personal bias or prejudice against the defendant such that the judge should have disqualified himself. Additionally, although the jury instruction on the presumption of innocence was misleading, the court found that the outcome of the trial was not likely to be different without this instruction, as the evidence of defendant's guilt was overwhelming. Counsels' isolated error did not warrant vacation of defendant's conviction in the face of the significant overall adversarial testing to which counsel subjected the State's case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's petition for post-conviction relief, finding that the court did not engage in what defendant called unconstitutional appellate sentencing, the post-conviction judge did not err by declining to disqualify himself, and defendant's trial and appellate counsel were not ineffective.

OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; the challenged findings were supported by the evidence and appellants raised no substantial questions for trial.

OVERVIEW: A jury found appellant guilty of four counts of murder. The trial court ordered the death sentence, upon the jury's recommendation. 188 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lombardo


Supreme Court No. 38S00-9902-CR-111


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


738 N.E.2d 653; 2000 Ind. LEXIS 1072



November 3, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE JAY CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Kenneth Sullivan, Special Judge. Cause No. 38C01-9707-CF-25.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the judgment of the Jay Circuit Court (Indiana) granting defendant's motion to dismiss the unlawful interception of a telephonic communication charge against him on the ground that the Indiana Wiretap Act, Ind. Code §§ 35-33.5-1-1 through 35-33.5-5-6, was unconstitutionally vague because it did not clearly define the conduct prohibited.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged for allegedly secretly tape recording his estranged wife's telephone conversations. The trial court dismissed the charge on the ground that the Indiana Wiretap Act (Act) was unconstitutionally vague. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that even though the Act was internally inconsistent regarding the degree of culpability required, a person of ordinary intelligence would know that the act of wiring a tape recorder to secretly record another's conversation was an intentional act clearly prohibited by the Act. The court held that the phrase "under this article" contained in Ind. Code § 35-33.5-1-5 limited the definition of "interception" to an application under the Act, and did not mean that the Act only outlawed interceptions by a computer or fax machine. The court held that the Act did not incorporate conflicting federal case law on intercepting the telephone communications of one's spouse within the marital home, but that rather the provision, Ind. Code § 35-33.5-5-5(a), provided an exemption for any wiretapping conducted by law enforcement under the Federal Wiretap Act.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed because the Indiana Wiretap Act (Act) was not unconstitutionally vague as it clearly prohibited the act of wiring a tape recorder to secretly record another's conversation, the Act did not outlaw only those interceptions accomplished by a computer or fax machine, and did not incorporate conflicting federal case law.

 

189 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Ellis v. State


No. 01S00-9910-CR-632


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


736 N.E.2d 731; 2000 Ind. LEXIS 973



October 18, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ADAMS CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 01C01-9808-CF-27. The Honorable Mark A. McIntosh.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and affirmed in part, and remanded for sentencing as indicated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment, based upon a jury verdict, of the Adams Circuit Court (Indiana), convicting him of murder, two counts of attempted murder, and burglary, and sentencing him to 165 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Appellant shot his wife, her stepfather, and another man in her company after appellant discovered his wife kissing this man. Appellant's wife died from her six gunshot wounds. The two men survived. The trial court imposed consecutive sentences of 65 years for murder and 50 years for each attempted murder. It also ordered a concurrent 20 sentence for burglary. Appellant asserted the trial court erred when it refused his tendered instructions on criminal recklessness and reckless homicide. The court disagreed. Appellant's mere assertion of an involuntary intoxication defense did not create a serious evidentiary dispute such that a jury could have concluded appellant did not commit murder, but instead committed the lesser included offense of reckless homicide. Trial court did not err in refusing to instruct the jury on criminal recklessness because it was neither inherently nor factually included in the crime charged. Trial court erred when it ordered appellant's sentences for the two counts of attempted murder to be served consecutively for a total term of 100 years. This portion of the sentence exceeded the statutory limitation. Thus, the case was remanded for re-sentencing.


OUTCOME: Convictions were affirmed, as trial court did not err by refusing to instruct the jury on reckless homicide and criminal recklessness as lesser included offenses of murder and attempted murder, respectively. Appellant did not prove he merely acted recklessly. Sentence was reversed in part and remanded, as consecutive sentences for two counts of attempted murder exceeded the statutory limitation.

 

190 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Indiana Dep't of State Revenue v. Farm Credit Servs. of Mid-America


Cause No. 49S10-9908-TA-453


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


734 N.E.2d 551; 2000 Ind. LEXIS 712



September 1, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE INDIANA TAX COURT. The Honorable Thomas G. Fisher, Judge. Cause No. 49T10-9801-TA-5.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the Indiana Tax Court decision granting summary judgment in appellee's favor, finding appellant immune from Indiana's Financial Institutions Tax under the doctrine of intergovernmental tax immunity.


OVERVIEW: Appellee agricultural credit association (ACA) was created through the merger of two production credit associations (PCA) and two federal land bank associations (FLBA). It was part of the farm credit system, a network of cooperative, borrower-owned banks established to provide affordable credit to farmers and ranchers. As an ACA, appellee claimed it was exempt from Indiana's Financial Institutions Tax under constitutional principles of intergovernmental tax immunity. The court reversed. As a merged association, appellee was a combination of the two previous entities. The resulting ACA continued to provide the same services. Appellee performed two autonomous functions: long-term mortgage lending through an FLBA and short-term lending through a PCA. Congress found long-term lending institutions, like FLBA's, were entitled to immunity while short-term lending institutions, like PCA's which were privately owned and controlled, were not entitled to immunity. Thus, appellant was entitled to tax only income derived from appellee's short-term PCA operations.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded for a determination of tax due on appellee's production credit association operations because the operations were privately owned and controlled, despite the merger.

Wright v. State


Cause No. 20S00-9808-CR-431


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


730 N.E.2d 713; 2000 Ind. LEXIS 651



July 3, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ELKHART CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 20C01-9706-CF-30. The Honorable Gene R. Duffin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Elkhart Circuit Court of murder, stemming from the killing of defendant's neighbor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder of his neighbor. Defendant appealed the conviction, arguing the trial court improperly instructed the jury on plaintiff State's burden of proof and statutory intoxication defense, that the trial court improperly admitted several photographs of victim into evidence, and other errors. The court held the reasonable doubt jury instruction given was proper. The instructions informed jurors that if they concluded beyond reasonable doubt that defendant was guilty, they should have returned verdict of guilty. The court held it was not improper to instruct the jury with regards to the word "should". The court held the evidence did not demonstrate that defendant was so intoxicated at the time of the crime as to prevent him from forming the requisite intent to murder. Several days after the murder, defendant gave police a comprehensive account of his activities. Defendant was alert enough to walk home, climb through a window, and wash blood from his hands and face. The court held the trial court properly admitted photographs of the victim. The photographs at issue established the cause of death and the manner in which the crime was committed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction, because the trial court properly instructed the jury on plaintiff State's burden of proof and a statutory intoxication defense, and properly admitted several photographs of the victim in to evidence.

Boggs v. Tri-State Radiology


Indiana Supreme Court Cause No. 82S04-0002-CV-115


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


730 N.E.2d 692; 2000 Ind. LEXIS 634



June 28, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Terry D. Dietsch, Judge. Cause No. 82D03-9710-CP-3553. Indiana Court of Appeals Cause No. 82A04-9809-CV-450.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Indiana Court of Appeals, which held the statute of limitations contained in the Medical Malpractice Act, Ind. Code § 34-18-8-4 (1998) was unconstitutional as applied to appellee, and reversed the judgment granting appellant's motion for preliminary determination of its statute of limitations defense.


OVERVIEW: Appellee's wife went to doctor after detecting a mass in her left breast. A mammogram was taken and interpreted by appellant radiology firm. Doctor instructed appellee's wife to return after one year. About a year later, a biopsy was performed based on a second mammogram. The mass was malignant, and the cancer had metastasized. Appellee's wife died a year later. Appellee brought suit under the Medical Malpractice Act (Act), Ind. Code § 34-18-8-4 (1998) against doctor and appellant. Appellant filed a motion for preliminary determination of its statute of limitations defense. The trial court granted appellant's motion, treating it as a motion for summary judgment, and granted judgment in appellant's favor. Appellee sought review. The appeals court reversed, and held that the statute of limitations within the Act was unconstitutional as it applied to appellee. Appellant sought further review. The supreme court reversed the court of appeals, and affirmed the trial court, as appellee had 11 months to bring an action after discovery of the injury, therefore, the Act did not unconstitutionally limit or bar appellee's possibility of relief.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order holding that the statute of limitations was unconstitutional as it applied to appellee, because appellee had 11 months to file a medical malpractice claim against appellant after knowledge of the injury, yet did not. The court affirmed the order granting the motion for a preliminary determination, as neither of the doctrines of fraudulent concealment nor continuing wrong applied.

State Bd. of Tax Comm'rs v. Montgomery


Indiana Supreme Court Cause No. 45S00-9906-TA-340


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


730 N.E.2d 680; 2000 Ind. LEXIS 635



June 27, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE INDIANA TAX COURT. The Honorable Thomas G. Fisher, Judge. Cause No. 45T10-9807-TA-84.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought interlocutory review of an order of the Indiana Tax Court, holding that it had subject matter jurisdiction over appellees' action, which sought a declaratory judgment that the Health Care for the Indigent program (HCI) violated Ind. Const. art. 10, § 1 and Ind. Const. art 1, § 23.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, a county, the county council, the county board of commissioners, and individuals on the board and council, brought suit in their official capacities and as taxpayers in tax court against appellants, the Indiana State Board of Tax Commissioners, seeking a declaratory judgment that the formula for calculating the tax levy for the Health Care for the Indigent program (HCI) violated Ind. Const. art. 10, § 1 and Ind. Const. art 1, § 23. Appellees contended that the statutory formula for setting the HCI tax levy resulted in a wide disparity between the contribution of county residents to the HCI state fund and the county's percentage of statewide assessed value. The tax court held that it had subject matter jurisdiction, despite appellants' contention that appellees had not exhausted administrative remedies. The issue was certified for interlocutory review, and the court granted appellants' petition for review. The court held that appellees were required to first exhaust the administrative remedy of requesting a refund, and that the tax court was without jurisdiction because no appellee had sought review of a final order of appellants.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded with direction to dismiss appellees' claim for declaratory relief, as appellees had to first exhaust the administrative remedy of requesting a refund, and that there was no jurisdiction, because no appellee had sought review of a final order of appellants.

 

194 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


McIntosh v. Melroe Co.


Indiana Supreme Court Cause No. 71S03-9805-CV-297


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


729 N.E.2d 972; 2000 Ind. LEXIS 489; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P15,814



May 26, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ST. JOSEPH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Jeanne Jourdan, Judge. Cause No. 71D07-9506-CT-00229. Indiana Court of Appeals Cause No. 71A03-9609-CV-320.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs filed a petition to transfer, appealing the judgment of the Indiana Court of Appeals, which affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment for defendant manufacturer, in a suit to determine whether the 10-year statute of repose, Ind. Code § 34-20-3-1(b), violated Ind. Const. art. I, §§ 12, 23.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sued defendants for injuries allegedly caused by a defect in a product manufactured by defendant manufacturer, which plaintiffs had purchased 13 years earlier. The state trial court granted defendant manufacturer's summary judgment motion based on the 10-year statute of repose, Ind. Code § 34-20-3-1(b). The state appellate court affirmed the decision. Plaintiffs filed a petition to transfer, arguing that the statute violated Ind. Const. art. I, §§ 12, 23. The state supreme court granted plaintiffs' transfer petition, and held that the statute was constitutional. First, the legislature had made the permissible legislative choice to limit product liability actions to the first 10 years of a product's use; thus, plaintiffs' injuries were not legally cognizable injuries for which a remedy existed. Second, the statute's disparate treatment was reasonably related to the class' inherent characteristics and did not distinguish among class members. Therefore, the grant of defendant manufacturer's motion was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The grant of defendant manufacturer's summary judgment motion was affirmed, on grounds that the statute of repose was constitutional. The legislature's choice to limit product liability actions to the first 10 years of a product's use was permissible, and the statute's disparate treatment was reasonably related to the class' inherent characteristics.

Town Council of New Harmony v. Parker


Cause No. 87S01-9911-CV-673 in the Supreme Court


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


726 N.E.2d 1217; 2000 Ind. LEXIS 300



April 18, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Order on Rehearing August 28, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Ind. LEXIS 713. As Corrected April 24, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE WARRICK CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Donald G. Hendrickson, Judge. Cause No. 87C01-9608-CP-305. Cause No. 87A01-9808-CV-305 in the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed judgment of the Warrick Circuit Court (Indiana) for plaintiff in her action alleging, inter alia, that failure to install various utilities at defendant town's expense and placing a chain across a street which accessed plaintiff's property both constituted violations of the Takings Clause of U.S. Const. amend. V.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sued defendant town, alleging, inter alia, that failure to install various utilities at defendant town's expense and placing a chain across a street which accessed plaintiff's property both constituted unlawful takings of property without just compensation in violation of the Takings Clause of U.S. Const. amend. V. The trial court agreed with plaintiff and entered judgment for her, which judgment the appellate court affirmed. On appeal, the court reversed. As to the placing of the chain across the street, the court held that plaintiff failed to present evidence that such action deprived her of access to her property or inconvenienced her more greatly than the general public, such that the action was not a taking of property. The court also held that defendant town did not take plaintiff's property when it asked her to pay a share of the cost of installing the utilities.


OUTCOME: Trial court's judgment was reversed. Court held that action of defendant town in asking plaintiff to pay a share of the cost of installing various utilities on plaintiff's property did not amount to an unconstitutional taking of plaintiff's property.

 

196 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Sanquenetti v. State


83S00-9802-CR-88


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


727 N.E.2d 437; 2000 Ind. LEXIS 295



April 14, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Cause No. 83C01-9703-CF-32. The Honorable Bruce V. Stengel, Judge. APPEAL FROM THE VERMILLION CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions and sentences in the Vermillion Circuit Court (Indiana) for the choking and stabbing murders of two people.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions and sentences for two choking and stabbing murders. He presented two claims of error: (1) that the accomplice liability statute, as applied, violated the privileges and immunities clause of the Indiana Constitution; and (2) that the trial court erred in imposing consecutive sentences without finding an aggravating circumstance. As to the first claim, the court found that current state law superceded the common law of criminal liability and thus the legal distinction between a principal and an accessory had ceased to exist. The court held that the first claim failed under the Collins test, so the statute, as applied, did not violate the privileges and immunities clause of the Indiana Constitution. Regarding the second claim, the court found that the trial court did not properly articulate the requirement to evaluate any aggravating circumstances used to impose consecutive sentences, but that the consecutive sentences were appropriate.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because accomplice liability statute did not violate the privileges and immunities clause of the Indiana Constitution, and, even though trial court's articulation fell short of the requirement that it evaluate any aggravating circumstances used to impose consecutive sentences, the court found consecutive sentences warranted.

Alexander v. Scheid


Indiana Supreme Court Cause No. 49S05-0004-CV-231


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


726 N.E.2d 272; 2000 Ind. LEXIS 248



April 3, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Indiana Court of Appeals. Cause No. 49A05-9710-CV-431. The Honorable Patrick L. McCarty, Judge. Cause No. 49D03-9612-CT-1631.



DISPOSITION: Transfer granted and reversed and remanded to trial court for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed a decision by the Indiana Court of Appeals which upheld a trial court decision granting summary judgment to defendants in plaintiff's action under the Indiana Medical Malpractice Act, Ind. Code §§ 27-12-10-1 to 26 (1993).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sued defendant under Indiana Medical Malpractice Act, Ind. Code §§ 27-12-10-1 to 26 (1993), alleging defendants failed to follow up on an x-ray that revealed a cancerous nodule in plaintiff wife's lung. When the complaint was filed, plaintiff was in remission. The trial court granted summary judgment to defendants, holding plaintiff wife suffered no present compensable injury, and the appellate court affirmed. The court held plaintiff could maintain a cause of action for increased risk of harm, described as decreased life expectancy or diminished probability of long-term survival. Plaintiff's medical experts testified the cancer would be incurable if plaintiff relapsed. The experts testified plaintiff's chances of complete recovery dropped significantly from the time of initial discovery to the date of diagnosis. The court held likelihood of death was not too remote or speculative an injury, and plaintiff wife should not be forced to wait for a relapse to sue.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the grant of summary judgment to defendants, because plaintiffs could pursue a medical malpractice claim in a situation where the injury, plaintiff wife's cancer, had not come to its full potential, and possibly never would.

Price v. State


Supreme Court No. 49S00-9802-CR-84


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


725 N.E.2d 82; 2000 Ind. LEXIS 208



March 16, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT, CRIMINAL DIVISION. The Honorable Z. Mae Jimison. Cause No. 49G20-9701-CF-6216.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision by the Marion Superior Court, Criminal Division (Indiana) convicting defendant and enhancing defendant's sentence for multiple counts of dealing in cocaine, possession of cocaine, dealing in marijuana, and possession of marijuana.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of dealing in cocaine, possession of cocaine, dealing in marijuana, and possession of marijuana. The trial court enhanced defendant's sentence by 30 years based upon a habitual offender finding. Defendant appealed, arguing that sentencing was erroneous, and plaintiff state erroneously excluded two eligible jurors based upon their age. The court held the trial court improperly considered two aggravating factors in enhancing the sentence. However, the court held the sentence was not based solely on those to factors. The trial court found six aggravating factors. The court held a single aggravating factor was sufficient to support the sentence enhancement. The court held the exclusion of jurors by plaintiff was proper. The court found age was a legitimate reason for the exercise of peremptory challenges in narcotics cases. The court held age was not a suspect classification with respect to the exercise of peremptory challenges.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, because valid aggravators existed supporting the trial court's decision to enhance the sentence, and plaintiff's state's use of peremptory challenges to exclude jurors based solely upon their age was proper.

 

199 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. State


Indiana Supreme Court Cause No. 49S00-9901-CR-46


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


725 N.E.2d 823; 2000 Ind. LEXIS 204



March 15, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Jane E. Barker, Judge Pro Tempore. Cause No. 49G06-9707-CF-104531.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged judgment from the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) after his conviction for murder and conspiracy to commit murder, alleging violations of speedy trial rights, his grant of immunity, and the hearsay rule.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, convicted of murder of and conspiracy to commit murder, appealed, contending that: (1) right to speedy trial under Ind. R. Crim. P. 4 was violated; (2) the trial court erred in overruling his immunity objection to the state's evidence; and (3) the trial court admitted inadmissible hearsay at trial. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The issue a defendant's right to a speedy trial was violated may not be raised for the first time on appeal; therefore, any claim of a violation of Ind. R. Crim. P. 4 was waived. A Kastigar hearing was not necessary. Defendant gave two statements to the police. Neither of these statements was subject to his grant of immunity. Testimony was not used to prove the truth of the matter asserted. Rather, a statement was used to show that there was prearrangement by other conspirators. As such it was not hearsay.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the trial court was affirmed. Defendant waived issue of violations of speedy trial by not objecting; immunity hearing was not required as defendant had made two statements to police not subject to his grant of immunity; testimony was admissible non-hearsay.

 

200 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Young v. State


Cause No. 49S00-9904-CR-242


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


725 N.E.2d 78; 2000 Ind. LEXIS 207



March 14, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Nancy L. Broyles, Master Commissioner. Cause No. 49G04-9804-CF-058703.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) convicting him of robbery as a class A felony, Ind. Code Ann. § 35-42-5-1 (West 1998), and imposing a presumptive sentence of 30 years and adding 30 years because appellant was a habitual offender.


OVERVIEW: Appellant entered victim's home. Appellant shoved victim and grabbed his billfold. Victim pursued appellant, and reached into the open window of appellant's getaway car to turn off the ignition. Appellant rapped his knuckles with a screwdriver and drove down the alley, but victim hung onto the car. Victim eventually fell off and appellant ran over his leg as he sped away. The snatching of money, exertion of force, and escape were so closely connected in time, place, and continuity that appellant's taking of property included the force used in his escape; thus, it was a robbery. Victim, a 69-year-old man, suffered a fractured ankle and badly lacerated arms and legs. That was substantial probative evidence from which factfinder could reasonably find serious bodily injury to convict appellant of a class A felony robbery. Relying on the gravity of the offense and the severity and numerosity of the predicate offenses, appellant's sentence was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; appellant committed robbery by use of force because force used in escape was closely connected to taking in time, place, and continuity. It was class A felony robbery because victim suffered serious bodily injury. Sentence affirmed because of gravity of offense and severity and numerosity of previous offenses.
